PlanPrompt - QUERY:

# Instructions
The available knowledge is insufficient to assess the Claim. Therefore, **propose a set of actions** to retrieve new and helpful evidence. Adhere to the following rules:
* The actions available are listed under Valid Actions, including a short description for each action. No other actions are possible at this moment. 
* For each action, use the formatting as specified in Valid Actions.
* Include all actions in a single Markdown code block at the end of your answer.
* Propose as few actions as possible, but as much as needed. Do not propose similar or previously used actions.



## Valid Actions
* `reverse_search`
   * Description: Performs a reverse image search to find similar images on the web.
   * How to use: Provide an image and the model will perform a reverse search to find similar images.
   * Format: reverse_search(<image:k>), where `k` is the image's ID

* `image_search`
   * Description: Run an image search on Google to retrieve related images for a given query.
   * How to use: This is a helpful tool for fact-checking images. Use this to retrieve images associated with a specific keyword or phrase. Ensure that the query is clear and specific to improve search accuracy. If no relevant images are found, refine the query or use more descriptive terms.
   * Format: image_search("your image search query goes here")

* `geolocate`
   * Description: Performs geolocation to determine the country where an image was taken.
   * How to use: Provide an image and the model will determine the most likely countries where it was taken.
   * Format: geolocate(<image:k>), where `k` is the image's ID

# Example: reverse_search()

# Instructions
In order to find evidence that helps your fact-check, you just ran a web search which yielded a Search Result. **Your task right now is to summarize the Search Result.** What to include:
* information that might be useful for the fact-check (see Record)
* relevant images (refer to images by inserting their reference <image:k>)
* if available: the release date as well as the author or the publisher (e.g. the media company) of the search result.

Do NOT include:
* advertisements
* any other information not related to the Record or the Claim

Additional rules:
* Do not add any additional information besides the information in the Search Result.
* If the Search Result doesn't contain any relevant information for the fact-checking work, simply print one word in capital letters: "NONE".
* Keep your writing style like in the Examples 1, 2 and 3 provided to you.
* Try to filter out relevant information even if the search result is in a different language.

Hollywood stars in Ukraine allegedly paid by USAID: a Kremlin-linked disinformation campaign and the ineffectiveness of Twitter Community Notes
===============================================================================================================================================

Publicado el Feb 7, 2025, 7:18:57‚ÄØPM Actualizado el Feb 7, 2025, 7:19:10‚ÄØPM

Tiempo de lectura: 12 minutos

! <image:6456>

Compartir:

Claves:

*   The disinformation campaign that claims that the United States Agency for International Development (USAID) has paid for celebrities to visit Ukraine has spread in at least nine languages
*   Maldita.es has analyzed more than 40 Twitter posts (now X) with this narrative that, in just three days, has more than 20 million views and only 14% have a note from the community denying it
*   Channels and websites linked to the Kremlin have published this disinformation narrative since the first day it began to be distributed

  

* * *

The video claiming that the United States Agency for International Development (USAID) [has paid for visits by several prominent US officials to Ukraine](https://maldita.es/malditobulo/20250206/video-angelina-jolie-orlando-bloom-visita-ucrania/)
 has gone viral with (fake) messages **in at least nine different languages** ‚Äã‚Äã(German, Spanish, French, English, Italian, Polish, Portuguese, Dutch and Romanian). Its impact has thus crossed borders, reaching more than 20 million views [on Twitter (now X)](https://maldita.es/malditatecnologia/20230724/twitter-x-cambio-nombre-logo-elon-musk/)
 in just three days.

[üì≤ ¬°Pincha aqu√≠ y sigue el canal de WhatsApp de Maldita.es  \
para que no te la cuelen!](https://bit.ly/3EGa2ju)

For this study, [Maldita.es](https://Maldita.es)
 has analysed [more than 40 posts](https://docs.google.com/spreadsheets/d/1gRE1WgvW3L5ECNejPxnxvudHNbJJQpdIW3HINA9UCo4/edit?gid=0#gid=0)
 (all of them with more than 5,000 views at 5pm on 7 February 2025) that spread this video with disinformation messages through X. These contents have been published over three days (between 5 and 7 February) and, together, they add up to millions of views on the platform. Even so, only 14.3% (that is, six out of 42) have [community notes](https://maldita.es/malditatecnologia/20240917/notas-de-la-comunidad-twitter-x/)
 warning users that it is disinformation content.

! <image:6457>

The narrative was also widely disseminated by channels and websites linked to or close to the Kremlin, both in Spain and in Russia and other countries between February 5 and 7.

**This disinformation narrative has 20 million views in three days and nine languages**
---------------------------------------------------------------------------------------

**The narrative shared in X:** USAID has sponsored visits by American celebrities (such as Angelina Jolie, Ben Stiller, Orlando Bloom, Sean Penn, and Jean-Claude Van Damme) to Ukraine since the Russian invasion began, in order to boost Ukrainian President Volodymyr Zelensky‚Äôs popularity in the United States and better coordinate its funding programs. Much of the content provides as supposed ‚Äúproof‚Äù a video with the logo of [E!News, a ‚Äúcelebrity and entertainment news‚Äù website in the United States](https://archive.ph/s1f93)
.

**The fact-check:** [The video circulating is not from E!News](https://maldita.es/malditobulo/20250206/video-angelina-jolie-orlando-bloom-visita-ucrania/)
. There is also [**no evidence**](https://maldita.es/malditobulo/20250206/video-angelina-jolie-orlando-bloom-visita-ucrania/)
 **of USAID's alleged payments to the celebrities it mentions.** Ben Stiller, the American actor and comedian who is the subject of the disinformation, has said that it is ‚Äúcompletely false.‚Äù

Even so, [Maldita.es](https://Maldita.es)
 [has located up to 42 contents with more than 5,000 views](https://docs.google.com/spreadsheets/d/1gRE1WgvW3L5ECNejPxnxvudHNbJJQpdIW3HINA9UCo4/edit?gid=0#gid=0)
 as of February 7 that spread this narrative on X. These have been published between February 5 and 7, 2025 and are shared in at least seven languages ‚Äã‚Äãin addition to Spanish: German, French, English, Italian, Polish, Portuguese, Dutch and Romanian. Some [have several million views](https://archive.ph/xuARn)
 and, together (and in just three days), they add up to more than 20 million views within this platform alone.

**Channels and websites linked to the Kremlin have been publishing this disinformation narrative since February 5**
-------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------

Since February 5, social media channels linked to the Kremlin or that routinely share disinformation pushed by Russia have also been spreading the video accusing USAID of paying Hollywood stars to travel to Ukraine.

On February 5, the X account ‚ÄúRussia Informa,‚Äù which has almost 80,000 followers, [shared the video](https://archive.li/OMGEP)
 with claims such as ‚ÄúUSAID paid Hollywood stars to visit Kyiv after the start of the special operation. The E!News portal published the details. Angelina Jolie cost the most: 20 million.‚Äù Also [the Telegram channel](https://archive.ph/NEJeQ)
 ‚ÄúIrinamar,‚Äù which claims to share content with a ‚ÄúRussian view of the special operation in Ukraine,‚Äù or ‚Äú[Wars and Geopolitics](https://archive.ph/rTjNU)
‚Äù, among others, published a post that same day.

On February 6, it was shared **by the website Spanish News Pravda**, a website that is part of the Pravda ecosystem and that, according to the [Viginum agency](https://www.sgdsn.gouv.fr/notre-organisation/composantes/service-de-vigilance-et-protection-contre-les-ingerences-numeriques)
, belonging to the General Secretariat of National Defense and Security of France, ‚Äúone of its main objectives is to spread disinformation and pro-Russian propaganda in different EU languages‚Äù. In Spain, [Spanish News Pravda has published](https://maldita.es/index.php/malditobulo/20241106/comitiva-rey-paginas-rusas-arabe/)
 disinformation such as the hoax about Felipe VI‚Äôs motorcade in Valencia after the passage of the DANA [or the hoax that Coca-Cola had donated mobile morgues](https://maldita.es/malditobulo/20241203/morgue-mobile-cocacola-ucrania/)
 with its logo to Ukraine. On this occasion, Spanish News Pravda published it on two occasions ([1](https://archive.ph/bqahS)
 and [2](https://archive.li/PdxYX)
).

Liu Sivaya [also shared the E!News video](https://archive.li/2hpjN)
 on the 6th on her X account, where she has nearly 200,000 followers.

! <image:6464>

Between February 5 and 6, it was also actively disseminated ‚Äúby Russian propaganda outlets, including Tsargrad, Russia Today, EurAsia Daily, Rossiyskaya Gazeta, Military Review, and Vesti,‚Äù explain Georgian fact-checkers [Myth Detector, who have also verified the content](https://mythdetector.com/en/usaid-paid-actors/)
. They add that it was shared not only by Kremlin-controlled outlets, ‚Äúbut also by networks affiliated with the Georgian government, including the pro-government POSTV, several media channels, as well as individual accounts,‚Äù as they identify in the published article.

! <image:6465>

**Only six of the 42 disinformation contents have Community Notes**
-------------------------------------------------------------------

At the time of publication of this text, 85.7% of the contents analysed (i.e. 37 out of 42) **are circulating on X without** [**community notes**](https://maldita.es/malditatecnologia/20240917/notas-de-la-comunidad-twitter-x/)
. Only in six of the more than 40 cases does the warning system of Elon Musk's platform indicate that they are disinformation content. These posts are written in Spanish (3), German (1), French (1) and English (1). None of the contents with more than 5,000 views that have been taken into account in this analysis in Italian, Polish, Portuguese, Dutch or Romanian contain these messages.

! <image:6466>

Those cases in which the Community Notes have been applied do not reach 125.000 views in any single post. In fact, [the tweet with the most impact](https://archive.ph/xuARn)
 that [Maldita.es](https://Maldita.es)
 has found with this narrative (which has, as of the date of publication of this text, more than 15.8 million views) [**does not have a visible warning**](https://maldita.es/malditobulo/20250207/ben-stiller-tuit-desinformador-nota-comunidad/)
**,** more than 36 hours after its publication. It is the first post in a thread in English that states that ‚ÄúUSAID paid Ben Stiller 4 million dollars to take these photos with Zelensky.‚Äù This message is accompanied by two images (which are real) of the American actor and comedian with the president of Ukraine.

! <image:6467>

[Community Notes is the system implemented](https://maldita.es/nosotros/20250117/notas-comunidad-verificadores-juntos-funcione/)
 in X that allows users to add context to misleading tweets. [Although this is only selected and displayed when it is rated](https://maldita.es/malditatecnologia/20240917/notas-de-la-comunidad-twitter-x/#:~:text=en%20la%20desinformaci%C3%B3n%3F-,%C2%BFC%C3%B3mo%20funcionan%20las%20Notas%20de%20la%20comunidad%3F,-Las%20Notas%20de)
 as useful by enough contributors with ‚Äúdifferent points of view.‚Äù In fact**,** [**there are actually notes proposed**](https://archive.is/QieM8)
 **in the tweet with more than 15.8 million views**, as mentioned above. And why are they not displayed? Due to a lack of consensus between contributors, who present ‚Äúdifferent points of view‚Äù according to the platform‚Äôs rules.

! <image:6468>

This is precisely one of the points to improve the X Community Notes system identified by [Maldita.es](https://Maldita.es)
 [in its analysis](https://maldita.es/nosotros/20250117/notas-comunidad-verificadores-juntos-funcione/)
. One of the problems it raises is that many of the notes that are proposed and that refute viral misinformation are never shown to users. It also points against the need for consensus among users, who tend to disagree.¬†

Thus, several contexts have been identified in which community notes have not been sufficient to combat hoaxes. For example, [during the disinformation campaign](https://maldita.es/malditatecnologia/20241127/dana-notas-comunidad-x-twitter/)
 that emerged on social networks as a result [of the DANA of October 2024](https://maldita.es/malditobulo/20241030/bulos-y-desinformaciones-sobre-el-paso-de-la-dana-en-el-este-y-sur-de-espana-en-octubre-de-2024/)
: out of 176 tweets analysed with disinformation narratives about heavy rains, only 8.5% had visible community notes. They were also not enough to stop the spread of the [hoax of the video of the European Parliament applauding the launch of missiles from Ukraine to Russia](https://maldita.es/malditobulo/20241125/parlamento-europeo-aplausos-misiles-ucrania/)
. This content was spread in at least [five different languages on X](https://maldita.es/malditobulo/20241126/bulo-parlamento-europeo-misiles-europa/)
 and none of those analysed by [Maldita.es](https://Maldita.es)
 had community notes.

[¬øCrees que te ha llegado un bulo? Verifica en nuestro chatbot de WhatsApp (+34 644 229 319)](https://api.whatsapp.com/send?phone=34644229319&text=&source=&data=&app_absent=)

**61.9% of posts are from users with a blue tick, but that does not mean they are trustworthy**
-----------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------

A common factor detected in this analysis is that most of the accounts that have shared the narrative about USAID allegedly paying US celebrities to visit Ukraine in X **pay the premium version**. Of the 42 pieces of content analysed, **37 were published by users with the so-called** [**blue tick**](https://maldita.es/malditatecnologia/20230421/Twitter-tic-azul-original-cambios/)
 (61.9% of the total). In fact, among the ten most viral tweets, there is only one tweet that does not have the blue tick.

! <image:6469>

The blue tick is no longer synonymous with the fact that a profile is verified and is who it claims to be. Now, [this badge is obtained by paying a subscription](https://maldita.es/malditobulo/20230331/tic-azul-twitter-blue-desinformacion-cuentas-verificadas/)
 fee, so anyone can access it. This change may give a false sense of security to the user viewing the content on their device.

**This disinformative narrative is circulated in at least nine languages within X**
-----------------------------------------------------------------------------------

The contents that have had the greatest impact so far are those disseminated in English. Of the 42 analysed by [Maldita.es](https://Maldita.es)
, **13 have been published in English.** In total, they have had more than 18.4 million views (an average of 1.4 million per publication).¬†

! <image:6472>

The **content in French**, meanwhile, has an average of **106,000 views per tweet**. The nine tweets taken into account for this analysis reach almost one million reproductions (958,821 views in total).¬†

Although to a lesser extent and with less impact, content in Portuguese, Spanish, German and Romanian was also found. Four publications in each of these languages were used in this analysis. Of this group, those published in Portuguese and Spanish have had the greatest reach (with an average of 61,000 and 44,000 reproductions, respectively). There were also three tweets in Italian (with 44,000 total views) and two in Polish (with a total of 11,765 views) and one in Dutch (with 20,100 views).

These 42 pieces of content do not reflect the full impact of the dissemination of this narrative. During the analysis, [Maldita.es](https://Maldita.es)
 **has located dozens of tweets** in localized languages ‚Äã‚Äãwith less than 5,000 views. In addition, this misinformation [has been shared on X](https://maldita.es/malditobulo/20250206/video-angelina-jolie-orlando-bloom-visita-ucrania/#:~:text=El%20v%C3%ADdeo%20ha%20sido%20compartido%20en%20Twitter%2C%20ahora%20X%2C%20por%20Donald%20Trump%20Junior%20o%20Elon%20Musk)
 by Elon Musk, the owner of the platform with 216.4 million followers, and Donald Trump Junior, son of the US president, with 14.2 million followers on this social network.

Hollywood star Ben Stiller has met Ukraine's President Volodymyr Zelenskyy, telling the actor-turned-leader: "You are my hero."

The US actor, 56, who has been meeting with refugees in **[Poland](https://news.sky.com/topic/poland-6132)
** and **[Ukraine](https://news.sky.com/topic/ukraine-6556)
** since 18 June, shook hands with the wartime premier as they met in Kyiv.

**[UK would be 'right to prepare for war' - Ukraine war latest updates](https://news.sky.com/story/ukraine-news-live-war-russia-putin-eu-membership-12541713)
**

He told President Zelenskyy: "It's great honour for me. You are my hero. You quit a great acting career for this."

"Not so great as you," he replied.

But Stiller insisted: "What you have done, the way you rallied the country and for the world, it's really inspiring."

The actor spoke of his time visiting the war-torn country, and the devastation he had seen.

"I feel that it's hard to understand what's going on here if you haven't been here.

"We were talking about the actual impact of coming here. I just was in Irpin this morning, saw the level of destruction.

"You see it on TV, you see it on social media, it's something else to actually see it and feel it and then to talk to people. We have talked to a bunch of people."

!Ukraine's President Volodymyr Zelenskiy meets with Hollywood actor and Goodwill Ambassador Ben Stiller, as Russia's attack on Ukraine continues, in Kyiv, Ukraine June 20, 2022. Ukrainian Presidential Press Service/Handout via REUTERS ATTENTION EDITORS - THIS IMAGE HAS BEEN SUPPLIED BY A THIRD PARTY.\
 <image:6474>

Image: Stiller told the Ukrainian leader: 'What you have done, the way you rallied the country and for the world, it's really inspiring.'

Located not far from Kyiv, Irpin saw heavy Russian bombardment earlier in the war but fierce defence by Ukrainian troops **[ensured that Kremlin forces got no closer to the capital](https://news.sky.com/story/ukraine-war-just-21-seconds-without-an-attack-inside-irpin-the-bombarded-town-that-resisted-a-russian-onslaught-12579091)
**.

The pair discussed the difficulties keeping the war in Ukraine in the global public eye after so many months of fighting.

President Zelenskyy said: "It is not interesting to speak about the war every day for an audience, for different people, but for us it is very important.

"When people forget to speak about this influence and how to push Russia, it's very difficult."

Looking at Stiller, he added: "Thanks to people like you, we can do it."

In his message he said: "I'm here meeting people who've been impacted by the work and hearing how it's changed their lives.

"War and violence are devastating people all over the world. No one chooses to flee their home. Seeking safety is a right and it needs to be upheld for every person."

Last week Stiller, who is a UNHCR (United Nations High Commissioner for Refugees) goodwill ambassador, had flown to Rzeszow in southeastern Poland.

On Sunday he was also spotted walking in the western city of Lviv, which has come under attack by [**Russian**](https://news.sky.com/topic/russia-5803)
 forces during the months-long invasion but has remained relatively unscathed compared to the ferocious assaults in the east of the country.

On his Instagram page, Stiller said he was meeting families "whose lives have been torn apart by war and violence in [**Ukraine**](https://news.sky.com/topic/ukraine-6556)
".

2. Write one paragraph about which one of the Decision Options applies best. Include the most appropriate decision option at the end and enclose it in backticks like `this`.




## Decision Options
* `false`: The claim is not factually accurate. This is the case if one of the following three conditions is met:(1) The claim is demonstrably false when it is disproven by evidence from multiple and reliable sources,(2) The claim or image is taken out of context, i.e. the origin, content and/or meaning of a statement or an image is misrepresented. For example, an old claim or an old image is mispresented in a new context in a misleading way,(3) There is not enough evidence to verify the claim or the evidence is conflicting or self-contradictory.
* `true`: The claim is factually accurate when it is confirmed by evidence from multiple and reliable sources.
* `not enough information`: The fact-check does not contain sufficient information to come to an conclusion. For example,there is substantial lack of evidence or the evidence is inconclusive, conflicting or self-contradictory. In the case of a lack of evidence, state which information exactly is missing. In particular, if no RESULTS or sources are available, pick this decision.

# Record
## Claim
Claim: "<image:17> This image shows Ben Stiller and Ukrainian President Volodymyr Zelensky at their meeting on June 20, 2022, for which Stiller received $4 million from USAID."

## Actions
```
reverse_search(<image:17>)
image_search("Ben Stiller Volodymyr Zelensky meeting June 20 2022")
```

## Evidence
### Evidence from `reverse_search`
The image of Ben Stiller and Volodymyr Zelensky is found in multiple sources. One source, [Maldita.es](https://maldita.es/malditobulo/20250207/hollywood-disinformation-twitter-community-notes/), discusses a disinformation campaign claiming that USAID paid celebrities to visit Ukraine and states that the narrative that Ben Stiller was paid $4 million by USAID is false. Other sources, such as [Sky News](https://news.sky.com/story/ukraine-war-ben-stiller-visits-kyiv-and-tells-president-volodymyr-zelenskyy-you-are-my-hero-12636878) and [Deadline](https://deadline.com/2022/06/ukraine-zelensky-ben-stiller-visit-international-refugee-day-joe-biden-russia-war-1235048800/), report on Ben Stiller's visit to Kyiv and his meeting with Zelenskyy on June 20, 2022. <image:6456>, <image:6457>, <image:6464>, <image:6465>, <image:6466>, <image:6467>, <image:6468>, <image:6469>, <image:6472>, <image:6474>, <image:6477>, <image:6481>


### Evidence from `image_search`
The Los Angeles Times published an article about Ben Stiller's meeting with Volodymyr Zelensky (<image:7259>). The BBC News shows Ben Stiller meeting with Volodymyr Zelensky (<image:7260>).

The image shows Ben Stiller and Ukrainian President Volodymyr Zelensky (<image:7261>).


## Elaboration
The claim that the image shows Ben Stiller and Ukrainian President Volodymyr Zelensky at their meeting on June 20, 2022, is supported by the evidence. Multiple sources confirm the meeting took place on that date. However, the claim that Stiller received $4 million from USAID for the meeting is false, according to [Maldita.es](https://maldita.es/malditobulo/20250207/hollywood-disinformation-twitter-community-notes/).


# Your Judgement



===== > RESPONSE:  < =====
The image does show Ben Stiller and Volodymyr Zelensky meeting on June 20, 2022. However, the claim that Stiller received $4 million from USAID for the meeting is false.

`false`

PlanPrompt - QUERY:

# Instructions
The available knowledge is insufficient to assess the Claim. Therefore, **propose a set of actions** to retrieve new and helpful evidence. Adhere to the following rules:
* The actions available are listed under Valid Actions, including a short description for each action. No other actions are possible at this moment. 
* For each action, use the formatting as specified in Valid Actions.
* Include all actions in a single Markdown code block at the end of your answer.
* Propose as few actions as possible, but as much as needed. Do not propose similar or previously used actions.



## Valid Actions
* `reverse_search`
   * Description: Performs a reverse image search to find similar images on the web.
   * How to use: Provide an image and the model will perform a reverse search to find similar images.
   * Format: reverse_search(<image:k>), where `k` is the image's ID

* `image_search`
   * Description: Run an image search on Google to retrieve related images for a given query.
   * How to use: This is a helpful tool for fact-checking images. Use this to retrieve images associated with a specific keyword or phrase. Ensure that the query is clear and specific to improve search accuracy. If no relevant images are found, refine the query or use more descriptive terms.
   * Format: image_search("your image search query goes here")

* `geolocate`
   * Description: Performs geolocation to determine the country where an image was taken.
   * How to use: Provide an image and the model will determine the most likely countries where it was taken.
   * Format: geolocate(<image:k>), where `k` is the image's ID

# Instructions
You just retrieved new Evidence. Now, **analyze the Claim's veracity using the evidence**. Always adhere to the following rules:
* Focus on developing new insights. Do not repeat larger parts from the Record. Do not restate the Claim.

# Record
## Claim
Claim: "<image:18> This image shows an authentic list realeased by Ukraine showing US politicians taking bribes from Ukraine. The highest bribe was 92 Million US-$ for Joe Biden."

## Actions
```
image_search("Joe Biden Mitch McConnell Nancy Pelosi net worth")
image_search("US politicians Ukraine bribes")
```

## Evidence
### Evidence from `image_search`
Roll Call published an article about the net worth of key lawmakers in 2015, including Nancy Pelosi, Mitch McConnell, and John Cornyn, with a graphic showing their minimum net worth (<image:7275>). The Wisconsin Examiner published an image of Mitch McConnell and Nancy Pelosi (<image:7277>).


### Evidence from `image_search`
The Guardian published an article on June 16, 2023, about Ukraine battling corruption, including a picture of Joe Biden and Volodymyr Zelensky (<image:6943>). Al Jazeera published an article about corruption in the US (<image:6944>). The Human Rights Watch published an article on July 24, 2025, about a new Ukrainian law that undermines the independence of anti-corruption bodies (<image:6945>).

The articles can be found here: [The Guardian](https://www.theguardian.com/world/2023/jun/16/as-well-as-fighting-russia-ukrainians-are-battling-corruption-at-home), [Al Jazeera](https://www.aljazeera.com/opinions/2023/9/28/corruption-is-as-american-as-apple-pie), and [Human Rights Watch](https://www.hrw.org/news/2025/07/24/ukraine-new-law-undercuts-independence-of-anti-corruption-bodies).


# Your Analysis



===== > RESPONSE:  < =====
The evidence includes articles about corruption in Ukraine and the US, as well as images of US politicians. However, there is no evidence to support the claim that the image shows an authentic list released by Ukraine detailing bribes taken by US politicians. The evidence does not mention any such list or provide any information about US politicians taking bribes from Ukraine.

JudgePrompt - QUERY:

# Instructions
**Determine the Claim's veracity** by following these steps:
1. Briefly summarize the key insights from the fact-check (see Record) in at most one paragraph.
2. Write one paragraph about which one of the Decision Options applies best. Include the most appropriate decision option at the end and enclose it in backticks like `this`.




## Decision Options
* `false`: The claim is not factually accurate. This is the case if one of the following three conditions is met:(1) The claim is demonstrably false when it is disproven by evidence from multiple and reliable sources,(2) The claim or image is taken out of context, i.e. the origin, content and/or meaning of a statement or an image is misrepresented. For example, an old claim or an old image is mispresented in a new context in a misleading way,(3) There is not enough evidence to verify the claim or the evidence is conflicting or self-contradictory.
* `true`: The claim is factually accurate when it is confirmed by evidence from multiple and reliable sources.
* `not enough information`: The fact-check does not contain sufficient information to come to an conclusion. For example,there is substantial lack of evidence or the evidence is inconclusive, conflicting or self-contradictory. In the case of a lack of evidence, state which information exactly is missing. In particular, if no RESULTS or sources are available, pick this decision.

## Valid Actions
* `reverse_search`
   * Description: Performs a reverse image search to find similar images on the web.
   * How to use: Provide an image and the model will perform a reverse search to find similar images.
   * Format: reverse_search(<image:k>), where `k` is the image's ID

* `image_search`
   * Description: Run an image search on Google to retrieve related images for a given query.
   * How to use: This is a helpful tool for fact-checking images. Use this to retrieve images associated with a specific keyword or phrase. Ensure that the query is clear and specific to improve search accuracy. If no relevant images are found, refine the query or use more descriptive terms.
   * Format: image_search("your image search query goes here")

* `geolocate`
   * Description: Performs geolocation to determine the country where an image was taken.
   * How to use: Provide an image and the model will determine the most likely countries where it was taken.
   * Format: geolocate(<image:k>), where `k` is the image's ID

JudgePrompt - QUERY:

# Instructions
**Determine the Claim's veracity** by following these steps:
1. Briefly summarize the key insights from the fact-check (see Record) in at most one paragraph.
2. Write one paragraph about which one of the Decision Options applies best. Include the most appropriate decision option at the end and enclose it in backticks like `this`.




## Decision Options
* `false`: The claim is not factually accurate. This is the case if one of the following three conditions is met:(1) The claim is demonstrably false when it is disproven by evidence from multiple and reliable sources,(2) The claim or image is taken out of context, i.e. the origin, content and/or meaning of a statement or an image is misrepresented. For example, an old claim or an old image is mispresented in a new context in a misleading way,(3) There is not enough evidence to verify the claim or the evidence is conflicting or self-contradictory.
* `true`: The claim is factually accurate when it is confirmed by evidence from multiple and reliable sources.
* `not enough information`: The fact-check does not contain sufficient information to come to an conclusion. For example,there is substantial lack of evidence or the evidence is inconclusive, conflicting or self-contradictory. In the case of a lack of evidence, state which information exactly is missing. In particular, if no RESULTS or sources are available, pick this decision.

The India Today article ([https://www.indiatoday.in/world/story/limousine-from-vladimir-putins-fleet-explodes-in-moscow-catches-fire-report-2701228-2025-03-30](https://www.indiatoday.in/world/story/limousine-from-vladimir-putins-fleet-explodes-in-moscow-catches-fire-report-2701228-2025-03-30)) and Northeast Live TV ([https://northeastlivetv.com/topnews/putins-2-75-lakh-luxury-limo-explodes/](https://northeastlivetv.com/topnews/putins-2-75-lakh-luxury-limo-explodes/)) report on the explosion. The Financial Express article ([https://www.financialexpress.com/world-news/limousine-from-putins-official-car-fleet-explodes-near-fsb-secret-service-headquarters-details-inside/3793071/](https://www.financialexpress.com/world-news/limousine-from-putins-official-car-fleet-explodes-near-fsb-secret-service-headquarters-details-inside/3793071/)) does not provide any content.

Therefore, the claim cannot be verified based on the available evidence. More information is needed to confirm Putin's presence in the car and his death.


## Actions
```
image_search("Vladimir Putin death explosion")
```

## Evidence
### Evidence from `image_search`
Al Jazeera reports on Vladimir Putin offering condolences after the presumed death of Yevgeny Prigozhin (<image:7292>). PBS reports on Russia accusing Ukraine of a failed assassination attempt on Putin (<image:7293>).


## Elaboration
The new evidence provides conflicting information. Al Jazeera reports on Putin offering condolences, implying he is alive. PBS reports on a failed assassination attempt on Putin, also implying he is alive.

The claim that Putin died in an explosion is not supported by the new evidence.


# Your Judgement



===== > RESPONSE:  < =====
The initial search revealed that a limousine from Vladimir Putin's fleet exploded, but there was no information about Putin's presence or death. Subsequent searches showed reports of Putin offering condolences and a failed assassination attempt, which contradict the claim.

The claim is demonstrably false because the evidence suggests that Putin is alive. `false`

## Elaboration
The evidence indicates that a limousine from Vladimir Putin's fleet exploded and caught fire in Moscow. However, the provided sources do not confirm that Putin was in the car or that he died in the explosion.

The India Today article ([https://www.indiatoday.in/world/story/limousine-from-vladimir-putins-fleet-explodes-in-moscow-catches-fire-report-2701228-2025-03-30](https://www.indiatoday.in/world/story/limousine-from-vladimir-putins-fleet-explodes-in-moscow-catches-fire-report-2701228-2025-03-30)) and Northeast Live TV ([https://northeastlivetv.com/topnews/putins-2-75-lakh-luxury-limo-explodes/](https://northeastlivetv.com/topnews/putins-2-75-lakh-luxury-limo-explodes/)) report on the explosion. The Financial Express article ([https://www.financialexpress.com/world-news/limousine-from-putins-official-car-fleet-explodes-near-fsb-secret-service-headquarters-details-inside/3793071/](https://www.financialexpress.com/world-news/limousine-from-putins-official-car-fleet-explodes-near-fsb-secret-service-headquarters-details-inside/3793071/)) does not provide any content.

# Instructions

## Valid Actions
* `reverse_search`
   * Description: Performs a reverse image search to find similar images on the web.
   * How to use: Provide an image and the model will perform a reverse search to find similar images.
   * Format: reverse_search(<image:k>), where `k` is the image's ID

* `image_search`
   * Description: Run an image search on Google to retrieve related images for a given query.
   * How to use: This is a helpful tool for fact-checking images. Use this to retrieve images associated with a specific keyword or phrase. Ensure that the query is clear and specific to improve search accuracy. If no relevant images are found, refine the query or use more descriptive terms.
   * Format: image_search("your image search query goes here")

* `geolocate`
   * Description: Performs geolocation to determine the country where an image was taken.
   * How to use: Provide an image and the model will determine the most likely countries where it was taken.
   * Format: geolocate(<image:k>), where `k` is the image's ID

JudgePrompt - QUERY:

# Instructions
**Determine the Claim's veracity** by following these steps:
1. Briefly summarize the key insights from the fact-check (see Record) in at most one paragraph.
2. Write one paragraph about which one of the Decision Options applies best. Include the most appropriate decision option at the end and enclose it in backticks like `this`.




## Decision Options
* `false`: The claim is not factually accurate. This is the case if one of the following three conditions is met:(1) The claim is demonstrably false when it is disproven by evidence from multiple and reliable sources,(2) The claim or image is taken out of context, i.e. the origin, content and/or meaning of a statement or an image is misrepresented. For example, an old claim or an old image is mispresented in a new context in a misleading way,(3) There is not enough evidence to verify the claim or the evidence is conflicting or self-contradictory.
* `true`: The claim is factually accurate when it is confirmed by evidence from multiple and reliable sources.
* `not enough information`: The fact-check does not contain sufficient information to come to an conclusion. For example,there is substantial lack of evidence or the evidence is inconclusive, conflicting or self-contradictory. In the case of a lack of evidence, state which information exactly is missing. In particular, if no RESULTS or sources are available, pick this decision.

# Record
## Claim
Claim: "In an interview with the Wall Street Journal, published on February 14, 2025, US Vice President J.D. Vance said the US military action is available against Russia."


CNN published an article about J.D. Vance on February 14, 2025, as stated in the article from [CNN](https://www.cnn.com/2025/02/14/politics/jd-vance-us-troops-russia-ukraine-intl-hnk). The Wall Street Journal published an article with an image of J.D. Vance, as stated in the article from [WSJ](https://www.wsj.com/opinion/jd-vance-makes-friends-with-britains-new-right-13880350). The search result contains an image of J.D. Vance, as stated in the article from [MSN](https://www.msn.com/en-us/money/companies/major-media-outlet-caught-twisting-jd-vance-s-words/ar-AA1z4AYf). <image:7304>, <image:7305>, <image:7306>

However, the evidence does not explicitly state whether J.D. Vance discussed US military action against Russia in the Wall Street Journal interview.

To verify the claim, I need to examine the content of the Wall Street Journal article.

JudgePrompt - QUERY:

# Instructions
**Determine the Claim's veracity** by following these steps:
1. Briefly summarize the key insights from the fact-check (see Record) in at most one paragraph.
2. Write one paragraph about which one of the Decision Options applies best. Include the most appropriate decision option at the end and enclose it in backticks like `this`.




## Decision Options
* `false`: The claim is not factually accurate. This is the case if one of the following three conditions is met:(1) The claim is demonstrably false when it is disproven by evidence from multiple and reliable sources,(2) The claim or image is taken out of context, i.e. the origin, content and/or meaning of a statement or an image is misrepresented. For example, an old claim or an old image is mispresented in a new context in a misleading way,(3) There is not enough evidence to verify the claim or the evidence is conflicting or self-contradictory.
* `true`: The claim is factually accurate when it is confirmed by evidence from multiple and reliable sources.
* `not enough information`: The fact-check does not contain sufficient information to come to an conclusion. For example,there is substantial lack of evidence or the evidence is inconclusive, conflicting or self-contradictory. In the case of a lack of evidence, state which information exactly is missing. In particular, if no RESULTS or sources are available, pick this decision.

PlanPrompt - QUERY:

# Instructions
The available knowledge is insufficient to assess the Claim. Therefore, **propose a set of actions** to retrieve new and helpful evidence. Adhere to the following rules:
* The actions available are listed under Valid Actions, including a short description for each action. No other actions are possible at this moment. 
* For each action, use the formatting as specified in Valid Actions.
* Include all actions in a single Markdown code block at the end of your answer.
* Propose as few actions as possible, but as much as needed. Do not propose similar or previously used actions.



## Valid Actions
* `reverse_search`
   * Description: Performs a reverse image search to find similar images on the web.
   * How to use: Provide an image and the model will perform a reverse search to find similar images.
   * Format: reverse_search(<image:k>), where `k` is the image's ID

* `image_search`
   * Description: Run an image search on Google to retrieve related images for a given query.
   * How to use: This is a helpful tool for fact-checking images. Use this to retrieve images associated with a specific keyword or phrase. Ensure that the query is clear and specific to improve search accuracy. If no relevant images are found, refine the query or use more descriptive terms.
   * Format: image_search("your image search query goes here")

* `geolocate`
   * Description: Performs geolocation to determine the country where an image was taken.
   * How to use: Provide an image and the model will determine the most likely countries where it was taken.
   * Format: geolocate(<image:k>), where `k` is the image's ID

# Example: reverse_search()

## Claim
Text: "<image:k> shows a rare event of a solar eclipse with a double ring."

...

## Actions
```
reverse_search(<image:k>)
```

```

```

JudgePrompt - QUERY:

# Instructions
**Determine the Claim's veracity** by following these steps:
1. Briefly summarize the key insights from the fact-check (see Record) in at most one paragraph.
2. Write one paragraph about which one of the Decision Options applies best. Include the most appropriate decision option at the end and enclose it in backticks like `this`.




## Decision Options
* `false`: The claim is not factually accurate. This is the case if one of the following three conditions is met:(1) The claim is demonstrably false when it is disproven by evidence from multiple and reliable sources,(2) The claim or image is taken out of context, i.e. the origin, content and/or meaning of a statement or an image is misrepresented. For example, an old claim or an old image is mispresented in a new context in a misleading way,(3) There is not enough evidence to verify the claim or the evidence is conflicting or self-contradictory.
* `true`: The claim is factually accurate when it is confirmed by evidence from multiple and reliable sources.
* `not enough information`: The fact-check does not contain sufficient information to come to an conclusion. For example,there is substantial lack of evidence or the evidence is inconclusive, conflicting or self-contradictory. In the case of a lack of evidence, state which information exactly is missing. In particular, if no RESULTS or sources are available, pick this decision.

PlanPrompt - QUERY:

# Instructions
The available knowledge is insufficient to assess the Claim. Therefore, **propose a set of actions** to retrieve new and helpful evidence. Adhere to the following rules:
* The actions available are listed under Valid Actions, including a short description for each action. No other actions are possible at this moment. 
* For each action, use the formatting as specified in Valid Actions.
* Include all actions in a single Markdown code block at the end of your answer.
* Propose as few actions as possible, but as much as needed. Do not propose similar or previously used actions.



## Valid Actions
* `reverse_search`
   * Description: Performs a reverse image search to find similar images on the web.
   * How to use: Provide an image and the model will perform a reverse search to find similar images.
   * Format: reverse_search(<image:k>), where `k` is the image's ID

* `image_search`
   * Description: Run an image search on Google to retrieve related images for a given query.
   * How to use: This is a helpful tool for fact-checking images. Use this to retrieve images associated with a specific keyword or phrase. Ensure that the query is clear and specific to improve search accuracy. If no relevant images are found, refine the query or use more descriptive terms.
   * Format: image_search("your image search query goes here")

* `geolocate`
   * Description: Performs geolocation to determine the country where an image was taken.
   * How to use: Provide an image and the model will determine the most likely countries where it was taken.
   * Format: geolocate(<image:k>), where `k` is the image's ID

Statista includes a graph showing the IMF's real GDP year-over-year growth estimates/projections in Russia, "As of Jan. 2025".

To verify the claim, I need to find the IMF's ranking of the world's largest economies in October 2024.

## Valid Actions
* `reverse_search`
   * Description: Performs a reverse image search to find similar images on the web.
   * How to use: Provide an image and the model will perform a reverse search to find similar images.
   * Format: reverse_search(<image:k>), where `k` is the image's ID

* `image_search`
   * Description: Run an image search on Google to retrieve related images for a given query.
   * How to use: This is a helpful tool for fact-checking images. Use this to retrieve images associated with a specific keyword or phrase. Ensure that the query is clear and specific to improve search accuracy. If no relevant images are found, refine the query or use more descriptive terms.
   * Format: image_search("your image search query goes here")

* `geolocate`
   * Description: Performs geolocation to determine the country where an image was taken.
   * How to use: Provide an image and the model will determine the most likely countries where it was taken.
   * Format: geolocate(<image:k>), where `k` is the image's ID

JudgePrompt - QUERY:

# Instructions
**Determine the Claim's veracity** by following these steps:
1. Briefly summarize the key insights from the fact-check (see Record) in at most one paragraph.
2. Write one paragraph about which one of the Decision Options applies best. Include the most appropriate decision option at the end and enclose it in backticks like `this`.




## Decision Options
* `false`: The claim is not factually accurate. This is the case if one of the following three conditions is met:(1) The claim is demonstrably false when it is disproven by evidence from multiple and reliable sources,(2) The claim or image is taken out of context, i.e. the origin, content and/or meaning of a statement or an image is misrepresented. For example, an old claim or an old image is mispresented in a new context in a misleading way,(3) There is not enough evidence to verify the claim or the evidence is conflicting or self-contradictory.
* `true`: The claim is factually accurate when it is confirmed by evidence from multiple and reliable sources.

# Instructions
In order to find evidence that helps your fact-check, you just ran a web search which yielded a Search Result. **Your task right now is to summarize the Search Result.** What to include:
* information that might be useful for the fact-check (see Record)
* relevant images (refer to images by inserting their reference <image:k>)
* if available: the release date as well as the author or the publisher (e.g. the media company) of the search result.

Do NOT include:
* advertisements
* any other information not related to the Record or the Claim

Additional rules:
* Do not add any additional information besides the information in the Search Result.
* If the Search Result doesn't contain any relevant information for the fact-checking work, simply print one word in capital letters: "NONE".
* Keep your writing style like in the Examples 1, 2 and 3 provided to you.
* Try to filter out relevant information even if the search result is in a different language.

# Instructions
In order to find evidence that helps your fact-check, you just ran a web search which yielded a Search Result. **Your task right now is to summarize the Search Result.** What to include:
* information that might be useful for the fact-check (see Record)
* relevant images (refer to images by inserting their reference <image:k>)
* if available: the release date as well as the author or the publisher (e.g. the media company) of the search result.

Do NOT include:
* advertisements
* any other information not related to the Record or the Claim

Additional rules:
* Do not add any additional information besides the information in the Search Result.
* If the Search Result doesn't contain any relevant information for the fact-checking work, simply print one word in capital letters: "NONE".
* Keep your writing style like in the Examples 1, 2 and 3 provided to you.
* Try to filter out relevant information even if the search result is in a different language.

# Example 1
The search result from America Today provides several photographs of the Notre-Dame Cathedral fire on April 15, 2019. <image:i>, <image:j>, <image:k>. None of the images show the Eiffel Tower in the background. 

# Example 2
NONE

# Example 3
The Guardian discusses a report blaming the Syrian government for a toxic gas attack and condemning their use of chemical weapons. The Guardian mentions the Chemical Weapons Convention and the responsibilities of Syria under the convention. According to The Guardian, The White House condemned the Assad regime for defying the norm against chemical weapons use.

–ò–º–µ–Ω–Ω–æ –æ—Å–≤–æ–±–æ–∂–¥–µ–Ω–∏–µ –ë–∞–ª–∞–∫–ª–µ–∏ –ø–æ–∑–≤–æ–ª–∏–ª–æ –í–°–£ –ª–∏—à–∏—Ç—å —Ä–æ—Å—Å–∏–π—Å–∫—É—é –≥—Ä—É–ø–ø–∏—Ä–æ–≤–∫—É, –∫–æ—Ç–æ—Ä–∞—è —Ç–∞–º —Å–∫–æ–Ω—Ü–µ–Ω—Ç—Ä–∏—Ä–æ–≤–∞–Ω–∞, –≤–æ–∑–º–æ–∂–Ω–æ—Å—Ç–∏ –¥–µ—Ä–∂–∞—Ç—å –æ–±–æ—Ä–æ–Ω—É, –ø–æ—Å–∫–æ–ª—å–∫—É –æ—Ç—Ä–µ–∑–∞–ª–æ –∏—Ö –æ—Ç ¬´–ª–æ–≥–∏—Å—Ç–∏—á–µ—Å–∫–æ–π –∞—Ä—Ç–µ—Ä–∏–∏¬ª –í–æ–ª—á–∞–Ω—Å–∫-–ë–æ–ª—å—à–æ–π –ë—É—Ä–ª—É–∫-–ö—É–ø—è–Ω—Å–∫-–ò–∑—é–º, –ø–æ –∫–æ—Ç–æ—Ä–æ–π –ø—Ä–æ–∏—Å—Ö–æ–¥–∏–ª–æ —Å–Ω–∞–±–∂–µ–Ω–∏–µ –∞—Ä–º–∏–∏, –æ–±—ä—è—Å–Ω—è–µ—Ç —ç–∫—Å–ø–µ—Ä—Ç. ¬´–ë–µ–∑ —Å–Ω–∞–±–∂–µ–Ω–∏—è –≤—Å—è —ç—Ç–∞ –º–∞—Å—Å–∞ –ª–∏—á–Ω–æ–≥–æ —Å–æ—Å—Ç–∞–≤–∞ –∏ —Ç–µ—Ö–Ω–∏–∫–∏, —Å–∫–æ–Ω—Ü–µ–Ω—Ç—Ä–∏—Ä–æ–≤–∞–Ω–Ω–∞—è –Ω–∞ –ò–∑—é–º—Å–∫–æ–º –Ω–∞–ø—Ä–∞–≤–ª–µ–Ω–∏–∏, –æ–∫–∞–∑–∞–ª–∞—Å—å –±—ã –Ω–µ –±–æ–µ—Å–ø–æ—Å–æ–±–Ω–æ–π¬ª, ‚Äî –≥–æ–≤–æ—Ä–∏—Ç –ö–æ–≤–∞–ª–µ–Ω–∫–æ.

–ü–æ —Å–ª–æ–≤–∞–º —Ä–æ—Å—Å–∏–π—Å–∫–æ–≥–æ –≤–æ–µ–Ω–Ω–æ–≥–æ —ç–∫—Å–ø–µ—Ä—Ç–∞ –Æ—Ä–∏—è –§–µ–¥–æ—Ä–æ–≤–∞, —É —Ä–æ—Å—Å–∏–π—Å–∫–∏—Ö –≤–æ–π—Å–∫ –Ω–∞ —ç—Ç–æ–º –Ω–∞–ø—Ä–∞–≤–ª–µ–Ω–∏–∏ ¬´–æ—á–µ–Ω—å –∫—Ä—É–ø–Ω—ã–µ –ø–æ—Ç–µ—Ä–∏¬ª: –Ω–µ —Ç–æ–ª—å–∫–æ —É–±–∏—Ç—ã–º–∏, –Ω–æ –∏ –ø–ª–µ–Ω–Ω—ã–º–∏: ¬´–∫–∞–∫ –º–∏–Ω–∏–º—É–º —Å–æ—Ç–Ω–∏ –ø–ª–µ–Ω–Ω—ã—Ö, –µ—Å–ª–∏ –Ω–µ –ø–∞—Ä–∞ —Ç—ã—Å—è—á¬ª.

–í–µ—Ä–æ—è—Ç–Ω–æ–µ –±–æ–ª—å—à–æ–µ –∫–æ–ª–∏—á–µ—Å—Ç–≤–æ –ø–ª–µ–Ω–Ω—ã—Ö –ø–æ–¥—Ç–≤–µ—Ä–∂–¥–∞—é—Ç –∏ –¥–≤–æ–µ –±—ã–≤—à–∏—Ö –≤–æ–µ–Ω–Ω–æ—Å–ª—É–∂–∞—â–∏—Ö —Ä–æ—Å—Å–∏–π—Å–∫–æ–π –∞—Ä–º–∏–∏. ¬´–ü—Ä–∏ —Å–ø–æ–Ω—Ç–∞–Ω–Ω–æ–º –æ—Ç—Å—Ç—É–ø–ª–µ–Ω–∏–∏ –æ—Å–æ–±–µ–Ω–Ω–æ –º–Ω–æ–≥–æ –ø–ª–µ–Ω–Ω—ã—Ö. –°–≤—è–∑–∏ –≤–Ω—É—Ç—Ä–∏ –ø–æ–¥—Ä–∞–∑–¥–µ–ª–µ–Ω–∏–π –Ω–µ—Ç. –ö—Ç–æ –≥–¥–µ –Ω–∞—Ö–æ–¥–∏—Ç—Å—è, –∫–æ–º–∞–Ω–¥–∏—Ä—ã –Ω–µ –≤—Å–µ–≥–¥–∞ –∑–Ω–∞—é—Ç. –°–æ–æ—Ç–≤–µ—Ç—Å—Ç–≤–µ–Ω–Ω–æ, –æ–± –æ—Ç—Å—Ç—É–ø–ª–µ–Ω–∏–∏ –Ω–µ –≤—Å–µ –º–æ–≥—É—Ç –∑–Ω–∞—Ç—å¬ª, ‚Äî –≥–æ–≤–æ—Ä—è—Ç –æ–Ω–∏. –ë—ã–≤—à–∏–π –≤–æ–µ–Ω–Ω–æ—Å–ª—É–∂–∞—â–∏–π –æ–¥–Ω–æ–≥–æ –∏–∑ —ç–ª–∏—Ç–Ω—ã—Ö –ø–æ–¥—Ä–∞–∑–¥–µ–ª–µ–Ω–∏–π –≤ —Ä–∞–∑–≥–æ–≤–æ—Ä–µ —Å ¬´–í–∞–∂–Ω—ã–º–∏ –∏—Å—Ç–æ—Ä–∏—è–º–∏¬ª –æ—Ç–º–µ—Ç–∏–ª, —á—Ç–æ –Ω–∞ –•–∞—Ä—å–∫–æ–≤—Å–∫–æ–º –Ω–∞–ø—Ä–∞–≤–ª–µ–Ω–∏–∏ –æ–±–µ —Å—Ç–æ—Ä–æ–Ω—ã –Ω–µ—Å—É—Ç –æ—â—É—Ç–∏–º—ã–µ –ø–æ—Ç–µ—Ä–∏. ¬´–ö–æ–≥–¥–∞ –º–æ–∏ –≥–æ–≤–æ—Ä—è—Ç: ‚Äû–ë–ª—è, —Ç–∞–º –ø–∏–∑–¥–µ—Ü‚Äú, –∑–Ω–∞—á–∏—Ç, —á—Ç–æ –≤—Å—ë –ø–ª–æ—Ö–æ¬ª, ‚Äî –¥–æ–±–∞–≤–∏–ª —Å–æ–±–µ—Å–µ–¥–Ω–∏–∫ ¬´–í–∞–∂–Ω—ã—Ö –∏—Å—Ç–æ—Ä–∏–π¬ª.

### **–ü–æ—á–µ–º—É –ø—Ä–æ–≤–∞–ª–∏–ª–∞—Å—å —Ä–æ—Å—Å–∏–π—Å–∫–∞—è –æ–±–æ—Ä–æ–Ω–∞**

–ù–µ—Å–º–æ—Ç—Ä—è –Ω–∞ —Ç–æ, —á—Ç–æ –≤ –•–∞—Ä—å–∫–æ–≤—Å–∫–æ–π –æ–±–ª–∞—Å—Ç–∏ –±—ã–ª–æ —Å–∫–æ–Ω—Ü–µ–Ω—Ç—Ä–∏—Ä–æ–≤–∞–Ω–æ –±–æ–ª—å—à–µ —Ä–æ—Å—Å–∏–π—Å–∫–∏—Ö –≤–æ–π—Å–∫, —á–µ–º –∑–∞–¥–µ–π—Å—Ç–≤–æ–≤–∞–Ω–æ —Å–∏–ª –í–°–£ –≤ –∫–æ–Ω—Ç—Ä–Ω–∞—Å—Ç—É–ø–ª–µ–Ω–∏–∏ –Ω–∞ —ç—Ç–æ–º —É—á–∞—Å—Ç–∫–µ, –æ–ø–µ—Ä–∞—Ü–∏—è –±—ã–ª–∞ –Ω–∞–ø—Ä–∞–≤–ª–µ–Ω–∞ –Ω–∞ –æ—Å–æ–±–æ —É—è–∑–≤–∏–º—ã–µ –º–µ—Å—Ç–∞, –≥–¥–µ –≤–æ–∑–º–æ–∂–Ω–æ—Å—Ç–∏ —Ä–æ—Å—Å–∏–π—Å–∫–∏—Ö –ø–æ–¥—Ä–∞–∑–¥–µ–ª–µ–Ω–∏–π –ø–æ –æ–±–æ—Ä–æ–Ω–µ –±—ã–ª–∏ –∏—Å—Ç–æ—â–µ–Ω—ã, –≥–æ–≤–æ—Ä–∏—Ç —É–∫—Ä–∞–∏–Ω—Å–∫–∏–π –≤–æ–µ–Ω–Ω—ã–π —ç–∫—Å–ø–µ—Ä—Ç –ê–ª–µ–∫—Å–∞–Ω–¥—Ä –ö–æ–≤–∞–ª–µ–Ω–∫–æ. ¬´–†–æ—Å—Å–∏–π—Å–∫–æ–µ –∫–æ–º–∞–Ω–¥–æ–≤–∞–Ω–∏–µ –∑–Ω–∞–ª–æ, —á—Ç–æ —É –Ω–∏—Ö –µ—Å—Ç—å —É—è–∑–≤–∏–º—ã–µ –º–µ—Å—Ç–∞ –≤ –•–∞—Ä—å–∫–æ–≤—Å–∫–æ–π –æ–±–ª–∞—Å—Ç–∏, –æ–Ω–∏ –¥–∞–∂–µ –ø—ã—Ç–∞–ª–∏—Å—å –∏—Ö –≤ –∑–Ω–∞—á–∏—Ç–µ–ª—å–Ω–æ–π —Å—Ç–µ–ø–µ–Ω–∏ —É—Å–∏–ª–∏—Ç—å. –ó–Ω–∞–ª–∏, –Ω–æ –ø—Ä–µ–¥–æ—Ç–≤—Ä–∞—Ç–∏—Ç—å \[–∏—Å—Ö–æ–¥ —Å–æ–±—ã—Ç–∏–π\] –Ω–µ –º–æ–≥–ª–∏: –Ω–µ—Ö–≤–∞—Ç–∫–∞ —Ä–µ—Å—É—Ä—Å–æ–≤ —É–∂–µ –Ω–∞—á–∞–ª–∞ —Å–∫–∞–∑—ã–≤–∞—Ç—å—Å—è –Ω–∞ –∏—Ö –≤–æ–∑–º–æ–∂–Ω–æ—Å—Ç—è—Ö –ø–æ –≤–µ–¥–µ–Ω–∏—é –æ–±–æ—Ä–æ–Ω—ã. –ò —Å–µ–π—á–∞—Å –º—ã –Ω–∞–±–ª—é–¥–∞–µ–º –∫–∞—Å–∫–∞–¥–Ω—ã–π –æ–±–≤–∞–ª –æ–±–æ—Ä–æ–Ω—ã¬ª, ‚Äî –æ–±—ä—è—Å–Ω—è–µ—Ç –ê–ª–µ–∫—Å–∞–Ω–¥—Ä –ö–æ–≤–∞–ª–µ–Ω–∫–æ.

*   [–ó–°–£ –≤–∂–µ –Ω–∞ –æ–∫–æ–ª–∏—Ü—è—Ö –æ–∫—É–ø–æ–≤–∞–Ω–æ–≥–æ –ö—É–ø‚Äô—è–Ω—Å—å–∫–∞](https://cripo.com.ua/news/war/zsu-vzhe-na-okolytsyah-okupovanogo-kup-yanska/ "Permalink to –ó–°–£ –≤–∂–µ –Ω–∞ –æ–∫–æ–ª–∏—Ü—è—Ö –æ–∫—É–ø–æ–≤–∞–Ω–æ–≥–æ –ö—É–ø‚Äô—è–Ω—Å—å–∫–∞")
    

–†–æ—Å—Å–∏–π—Å–∫–∏–π –≤–æ–µ–Ω–Ω—ã–π —ç–∫—Å–ø–µ—Ä—Ç –Æ—Ä–∏–π –§–µ–¥–æ—Ä–æ–≤ –≥–æ–≤–æ—Ä–∏—Ç, —á—Ç–æ –≤ –•–∞—Ä—å–∫–æ–≤—Å–∫–æ–π –æ–±–ª–∞—Å—Ç–∏ —É–∫—Ä–∞–∏–Ω—Å–∫–∞—è –∞—Ä–º–∏—è –∏—Å–ø–æ–ª—å–∑–æ–≤–∞–ª–∞ –Ω–æ–≤—É—é —Ç–∞–∫—Ç–∏–∫—É, –∫–æ—Ç–æ—Ä–∞—è –∏ –æ–±–µ—Å–ø–µ—á–∏–ª–∞ —É—Å–ø–µ—Ö –Ω–∞ —ç—Ç–æ–º –Ω–∞–ø—Ä–∞–≤–ª–µ–Ω–∏–∏. ¬´–í–°–£ –¥–µ–π—Å—Ç–≤—É—é—Ç –æ—á–µ–Ω—å –¥–∏–Ω–∞–º–∏—á–Ω–æ –∏ —Ñ–∞–∫—Ç–∏—á–µ—Å–∫–∏ –Ω–µ –∑–∞–¥–µ—Ä–∂–∏–≤–∞—é—Ç—Å—è –Ω–∞ —Ç–æ, —á—Ç–æ–±—ã —à—Ç—É—Ä–º–æ–≤–∞—Ç—å —Ç–µ –∏–ª–∏ –∏–Ω—ã–µ –≥–æ—Ä–æ–¥–∞. –û–Ω–∏ –ø—Ä–æ—Å—Ç–æ –∏—Ö –æ–±—Ö–æ–¥—è—Ç, –±–µ—Ä—É—Ç –≤ –∫–æ–ª—å—Ü–æ, –∏ —Ç–æ–≥–¥–∞ –≥–∞—Ä–Ω–∏–∑–æ–Ω—ã —ç—Ç–∏—Ö –≥–æ—Ä–æ–¥–∫–æ–≤ –∏ –Ω–µ–±–æ–ª—å—à–∏—Ö —Å–µ–ª –ø—Ä–æ—Å—Ç–æ –≤—ã–Ω—É–∂–¥–µ–Ω—ã –∫–∞–ø–∏—Ç—É–ª–∏—Ä–æ–≤–∞—Ç—å, ‚Äî —Ä–∞—Å—Å–∫–∞–∑—ã–≤–∞–µ—Ç —Ä–æ—Å—Å–∏–π—Å–∫–∏–π –≤–æ–µ–Ω–Ω—ã–π —ç–∫—Å–ø–µ—Ä—Ç –Æ—Ä–∏–π –§–µ–¥–æ—Ä–æ–≤.

‚Äî –°–µ–π—á–∞—Å —É–∂–µ –ø—Ä–∞–∫—Ç–∏—á–µ—Å–∫–∏ –≤–∑—è—Ç –ö—É–ø—è–Ω—Å–∫, –ø–æ –∫—Ä–∞–π–Ω–µ–π –º–µ—Ä–µ, —Ç–∞ —á–∞—Å—Ç—å, –∫–æ—Ç–æ—Ä–∞—è –Ω–∞—Ö–æ–¥–∏—Ç—Å—è –Ω–∞ –ø—Ä–∞–≤–æ–º –±–µ—Ä–µ–≥—É. –°–¥–∞–Ω –ò–∑—é–º –∏–ª–∏ –Ω–∞—Ö–æ–¥–∏—Ç—Å—è –≤ –ø—Ä–æ—Ü–µ—Å—Å–µ. –†–æ—Å—Å–∏–π—Å–∫–∏–µ –≤–æ–π—Å–∫–∞ —É—Ö–æ–¥—è—Ç –æ—Ç—Ç—É–¥–∞, —á—Ç–æ–±—ã –Ω–µ –ø–æ–ø–∞—Å—Ç—å –≤ –æ–∫—Ä—É–∂–µ–Ω–∏–µ. –≠—Ç–æ, –≤ –æ–±—â–µ–º, —Ä–∞–∑—É–º–Ω–æ–µ —Ä–µ—à–µ–Ω–∏–µ, –ø–æ—Ç–æ–º—É —á—Ç–æ –∫–æ–º–º—É–Ω–∏–∫–∞—Ü–∏–∏ –ø–µ—Ä–µ—Ä–µ–∑–∞–Ω—ã. –°–∞–º –ø–æ —Å–µ–±–µ –ò–∑—é–º –Ω–∞—Ö–æ–¥–∏—Ç—Å—è –Ω–∞ —Å—Ç—ã–∫–µ –¥–≤—É—Ö —Ä–µ–∫: –û—Å–∫–æ–ª –∏ –°–µ–≤–µ—Ä—Å–∫–∏–π –î–æ–Ω–µ—Ü. –ï—Å–ª–∏ –µ–≥–æ –æ–∫—Ä—É–∂–∏—Ç—å, —Å–∫–∞–∂–µ–º, —Å —Å–µ–≤–µ—Ä–æ-–≤–æ—Å—Ç–æ–∫–∞ –∏–ª–∏ —Å —Å–µ–≤–µ—Ä–∞, —Ç–æ –æ–Ω –ø—Ä–æ—Å—Ç–æ –±—É–¥–µ—Ç –æ—Ç—Ä–µ–∑–∞–Ω –æ—Ç –ø–æ–¥–≤–æ–∑–∞ –±–æ–µ–ø—Ä–∏–ø–∞—Å–æ–≤ –∏ –≤—Å–µ–≥–æ –ø—Ä–æ—á–µ–≥–æ, –∏ \[—Ä–æ—Å—Å–∏–π—Å–∫–∞—è –∞—Ä–º–∏—è\] –≤—ã–Ω—É–∂–¥–µ–Ω–∞ –±—É–¥–µ—Ç –∫–∞–ø–∏—Ç—É–ª–∏—Ä–æ–≤–∞—Ç—å. –ß—Ç–æ–±—ã —ç—Ç–æ–≥–æ –Ω–µ —Å–ª—É—á–∏–ª–æ—Å—å, –æ–Ω–∏ –ø—Ä–æ—Å—Ç–æ –≤—ã–≤–æ–¥—è—Ç –≤–æ–π—Å–∫–∞, –ø–æ–∫–∞ –µ—Å—Ç—å –≤–æ–∑–º–æ–∂–Ω–æ—Å—Ç—å¬ª.

–Æ—Ä–∏–π –§–µ–¥–æ—Ä–æ–≤ —Å—á–∏—Ç–∞–µ—Ç, —á—Ç–æ –í–°–£ —Ç–∞–∫—Ç–∏—á–µ—Å–∫–∏ –∏ –æ–ø–µ—Ä–∞—Ç–∏–≤–Ω–æ –ø–µ—Ä–µ–∏–≥—Ä–∞–ª–∏ —Ä–æ—Å—Å–∏–π—Å–∫–∏–µ –≤–æ–π—Å–∫–∞, –∫–æ—Ç–æ—Ä—ã–º –Ω–µ —Ö–≤–∞—Ç–∏–ª–æ —Ä–µ—Å—É—Ä—Å–æ–≤ –¥–ª—è —Å–¥–µ—Ä–∂–∏–≤–∞–Ω–∏—è —ç—Ç–æ–≥–æ –Ω–∞—Å—Ç—É–ø–ª–µ–Ω–∏—è. ¬´\[–°–Ω–∞—á–∞–ª–∞\] –±—ã–ª–∞ –ø—Ä–æ—Ä–≤–∞–Ω–∞ –æ–±–æ—Ä–æ–Ω–∞ –≤ —Ä–∞–π–æ–Ω–µ –ë–∞–ª–∞–∫–ª–µ–∏. –ê –∑–∞—Ç–µ–º —Ä–æ—Å—Å–∏–π—Å–∫–∏–µ –≤–æ–π—Å–∫–∞ –±—ã–ª–∏ —Ä–∞–∑–±—Ä–æ—Å–∞–Ω—ã –≥–∞—Ä–Ω–∏–∑–æ–Ω–∞–º–∏ –ø–æ —Ä–∞–∑–ª–∏—á–Ω—ã–º –≥–æ—Ä–æ–¥–∫–∞–º, —Å–µ–ª–∞–º. –≠—Ç–∏ –≥–∞—Ä–Ω–∏–∑–æ–Ω—ã —á–∞—Å—Ç–æ —Å–æ—Å—Ç–æ—è–ª–∏ –∏–∑ –†–æ—Å–≥–≤–∞—Ä–¥–∏–∏, –∞ —Ç–∞–∫–∂–µ –º–æ–±–∏–ª–∏–∑–æ–≤–∞–Ω–Ω—ã—Ö –∏–∑ —Ç–∞–∫ –Ω–∞–∑—ã–≤–∞–µ–º—ã—Ö –Ω–∞—Ä–æ–¥–Ω—ã—Ö —Ä–µ—Å–ø—É–±–ª–∏–∫.

–†–æ—Å–≥–≤–∞—Ä–¥–∏—è –≤ –ø—Ä–∏–Ω—Ü–∏–ø–µ –≤–æ–µ–≤–∞—Ç—å –Ω–µ —É–º–µ–µ—Ç, –æ–Ω–∞ –Ω–µ –¥–ª—è —ç—Ç–æ–≥–æ –ø—Ä–µ–¥–Ω–∞–∑–Ω–∞—á–µ–Ω–∞. –ó–∞–¥–∞—á–∞ —ç—Ç–∏—Ö –≥–∞—Ä–Ω–∏–∑–æ–Ω–æ–≤ –∏ –≥–≤–∞—Ä–¥–µ–π—Å–∫–∏—Ö –ø–æ–ª–∫–æ–≤ –∑–∞–∫–ª—é—á–∞–ª–∞—Å—å –≤ —Ç–æ–º, —á—Ç–æ–±—ã –¥–µ—Ä–∂–∞—Ç—å –≤ –ø–æ–¥—á–∏–Ω–µ–Ω–∏–∏ –º–µ—Å—Ç–Ω–æ–µ –Ω–∞—Å–µ–ª–µ–Ω–∏–µ. –ê —Å—Ä–µ–¥–∏ –º–æ–±–∏–ª–∏–∑–æ–≤–∞–Ω–Ω—ã—Ö –º–Ω–æ–≥–∏–µ –≤ –ø–µ—Ä–≤—ã–π —Ä–∞–∑ –≤–∑—è–ª–∏ –≤ —Ä—É–∫–∏ –∞–≤—Ç–æ–º–∞—Ç, –Ω–∞–¥–µ–ª–∏ –∫–∞—Å–∫—É, –º–æ—Ç–∏–≤–∞—Ü–∏–∏ \[—É –Ω–∏—Ö –Ω–µ—Ç\] –Ω–∏–∫–∞–∫–æ–π. –†–æ—Å—Å–∏–π—Å–∫–∏–µ —Ä–µ–≥—É–ª—è—Ä–Ω—ã–µ —á–∞—Å—Ç–∏ –±—ã–ª–∏ –æ—Ç–≤–µ–¥–µ–Ω—ã —á–∞—Å—Ç–∏—á–Ω–æ –Ω–∞ –ø—Ä–∞–≤–æ–±–µ—Ä–µ–∂—å–µ –≤ –•–µ—Ä—Å–æ–Ω—Å–∫—É—é –æ–±–ª–∞—Å—Ç—å, —á–∞—Å—Ç–∏—á–Ω–æ –Ω–∞ –î–æ–Ω–µ—Ü–∫–æ–µ –Ω–∞–ø—Ä–∞–≤–ª–µ–Ω–∏–µ, –≥–¥–µ –æ–Ω–∏ –ø—ã—Ç–∞–ª–∏—Å—å —à—Ç—É—Ä–º–æ–≤–∞—Ç—å –ø—Ä–∏–≥–æ—Ä–æ–¥ –î–æ–Ω–µ—Ü–∫–∞, –∑–∞–Ω—è—Ç—ã–π –í–°–£. –ü–æ—ç—Ç–æ–º—É –≤–æ—Ç —Ç–∞–∫–æ–π —Ä–∞–∑–≥—Ä–æ–º¬ª, ‚Äî –æ–±—ä—è—Å–Ω—è–µ—Ç –≤–æ–µ–Ω–Ω—ã–π —ç–∫—Å–ø–µ—Ä—Ç.

–≠—Ç–æ –∂–µ –ø–æ–¥—Ç–≤–µ—Ä–∂–¥–∞–µ—Ç –≤ —Ä–∞–∑–≥–æ–≤–æ—Ä–µ —Å ¬´–í–∞–∂–Ω—ã–º–∏ –∏—Å—Ç–æ—Ä–∏—è–º–∏¬ª –∏ —Ä–æ—Å—Å–∏–π—Å–∫–∏–π –≤–æ–µ–Ω–Ω–æ—Å–ª—É–∂–∞—â–∏–π, –∫–æ—Ç–æ—Ä—ã–π –±—ã–ª –Ω–∞ —ç—Ç–æ–º –Ω–∞–ø—Ä–∞–≤–ª–µ–Ω–∏–∏. ¬´\[–ü–æ–¥–≤–µ–¥–æ–º—Å—Ç–≤–µ–Ω–Ω—ã–µ\] –ú–∏–Ω–æ–±–æ—Ä–æ–Ω—ã \[–≤–æ–π—Å–∫–∞\], –≥—Ä—É–ø–ø–∏—Ä–æ–≤–∫–∞ –í–æ—Å—Ç–æ–∫, –≤—ã—à–ª–∏ —Å —ç—Ç–æ–≥–æ –Ω–∞–ø—Ä–∞–≤–ª–µ–Ω–∏—è –µ—â–µ –≤ –∏—é–ª–µ –≤ –ë–µ–ª–≥–æ—Ä–æ–¥—Å–∫—É—é –æ–±–ª–∞—Å—Ç—å. –ù–∞ —Ç–æ—Ç –º–æ–º–µ–Ω—Ç –≤ –ò–∑—é–º–µ —è –≤—Å—Ç—Ä–µ—á–∞–ª –ë–ê–†–°–æ–≤ (_–±–æ–µ–≤–æ–π –∞—Ä–º–µ–π—Å–∫–∏–π —Ä–µ–∑–µ—Ä–≤ —Å—Ç—Ä–∞–Ω—ã_¬†‚Äî¬†**–ü—Ä–∏–º. —Ä–µ–¥.**), –æ–ø–æ–ª—á–µ–Ω—Ü–µ–≤ –∏ –≤–æ–π—Å–∫–∞ –ü–í–û –ó–∞–ø–∞–¥–Ω–æ–≥–æ –æ–∫—Ä—É–≥–∞. –ü–æ—Å–ª–µ \[–∏—Ö\] –≤—ã—Ö–æ–¥–∞ –≤ –ò–∑—é–º –∑–∞—à—ë–ª –°–û–ë–† –∏ –û–ú–û–ù. –°–æ–æ—Ç–≤–µ—Ç—Å—Ç–≤–µ–Ω–Ω–æ, —Ç–∞–º –¥–µ–π—Å—Ç–≤–∏—Ç–µ–ª—å–Ω–æ –æ—Å—Ç–∞–ª–∏—Å—å —Ç–æ–ª—å–∫–æ ‚Äû–ë–ê–†–°–∏–∫–∏‚Äú, –æ–ø–æ–ª—á–µ–Ω—Ü—ã –∏ –†–æ—Å–≥–≤–∞—Ä–¥–∏—è¬ª, ‚Äî –≥–æ–≤–æ—Ä–∏—Ç –æ–Ω.

–ü–æ —Å–ª–æ–≤–∞–º —ç–∫—Å–ø–µ—Ä—Ç–∞ –§–µ–¥–æ—Ä–æ–≤–∞, —Ä–æ—Å—Å–∏–π—Å–∫–æ–µ –∫–æ–º–∞–Ω–¥–æ–≤–∞–Ω–∏–µ –ø—Ä–æ—Å—á–∏—Ç–∞–ª–æ—Å—å –≤ –æ—Ü–µ–Ω–∫–µ —Å–∏—Ç—É–∞—Ü–∏–∏, –∫–æ–≥–¥–∞ –ø–µ—Ä–µ–±—Ä–æ—Å–∏–ª–æ –±–æ–µ–≤—ã–µ —á–∞—Å—Ç–∏ —Å —é–≥–∞ –•–∞—Ä—å–∫–æ–≤—Å–∫–æ–π –æ–±–ª–∞—Å—Ç–∏ –Ω–∞ –¥—Ä—É–≥–∏–µ –Ω–∞–ø—Ä–∞–≤–ª–µ–Ω–∏—è –¥–æ –Ω–∞—á–∞–ª–∞ –∫–æ–Ω—Ç—Ä–Ω–∞—Å—Ç—É–ø–ª–µ–Ω–∏—è. ¬´–°—á–∏—Ç–∞–ª–æ—Å—å, —á—Ç–æ –≤ —Ä–∞–π–æ–Ω–µ —Ä–∞—Å–ø–æ–ª–æ–∂–µ–Ω–∏—è –∏–∑—é–º—Å–∫–æ–π –≥—Ä—É–ø–ø–∏—Ä–æ–≤–∫–∏ –Ω–∏—á–µ–≥–æ —Å—Ç—Ä–∞—à–Ω–æ–≥–æ —Å–ª—É—á–∏—Ç—å—Å—è –Ω–µ –º–æ–∂–µ—Ç. –ü—Ä–æ—Å—á–µ—Ç –∑–∞–∫–ª—é—á–∞–ª—Å—è –≤ —Ç–æ–º, —á—Ç–æ –Ω–µ –±—ã–ª–∞ –æ—Ü–µ–Ω–µ–Ω–∞ –≤–µ—Ä–æ—è—Ç–Ω–æ—Å—Ç—å —Ç–æ–≥–æ, —á—Ç–æ —É–∫—Ä–∞–∏–Ω—Å–∫–∏–µ –≤–æ–π—Å–∫–∞ –Ω–∞—á–Ω—É—Ç —Ç–∞–º –Ω–∞—Å—Ç—É–ø–ª–µ–Ω–∏–µ¬ª, ‚Äî –≥–æ–≤–æ—Ä–∏—Ç –§–µ–¥–æ—Ä–æ–≤.

¬´–†–æ—Å—Å–∏–π—Å–∫–æ–µ –∫–æ–º–∞–Ω–¥–æ–≤–∞–Ω–∏–µ —Å –ø—Ä–æ—Ñ–µ—Å—Å–∏–æ–Ω–∞–ª—å–Ω–æ–π —Ç–æ—á–∫–∏ –∑—Ä–µ–Ω–∏—è –æ—Ü–µ–Ω–∏–≤–∞—é—Ç –∫–∞–∫ –æ—á–µ–Ω—å —Å–ª–∞–±–æ–µ. –≠—Ç–æ –ª—é–¥–∏, –∫–æ—Ç–æ—Ä—ã–µ —É–º–µ—é—Ç –±—Ä–æ—Å–∞—Ç—å –≤ –±–æ–π –∑–Ω–∞—á–∏—Ç–µ–ª—å–Ω–æ–µ –∫–æ–ª–∏—á–µ—Å—Ç–≤–æ –∂–∏–≤–æ–π —Å–∏–ª—ã, –Ω–æ –æ—Ç—Å—É—Ç—Å—Ç–≤—É–µ—Ç –∏–Ω–∏—Ü–∏–∞—Ç–∏–≤–∞ –≤ –∏—Å–ø–æ–ª–Ω–µ–Ω–∏–∏ –ø—Ä–∏–∫–∞–∑–∞. –ù–∞–ø–∏—Å–∞–Ω–æ ‚Äû–∑–∞–Ω—è—Ç—å —Ç–∞–∫–æ–π-—Ç–æ –ø–µ—Ä–µ–∫—Ä–µ—Å—Ç–æ–∫‚Äú, –∞ –º–æ–∂–µ—Ç –±—ã—Ç—å, –ª—É—á—à–µ –∑–∞–Ω—è—Ç—å –¥—Ä—É–≥–æ–π –ø–µ—Ä–µ–∫—Ä–µ—Å—Ç–æ–∫ —Ä—è–¥—ã—à–∫–æ–º, –Ω–æ —ç—Ç–æ –Ω–µ–¥–æ–ø—É—Å—Ç–∏–º–∞—è –≤–µ—â—å, \[—Ç–æ–ª—å–∫–æ\] —Ç—É–ø–æ–µ —É–ø–æ—Ä–Ω–æ–µ –≤—ã–ø–æ–ª–Ω–µ–Ω–∏–µ –ø—Ä–∏–∫–∞–∑–∞¬ª, ‚Äî –¥–æ–±–∞–≤–ª—è–µ—Ç –æ–Ω.

¬´–ù–µ–ª—å–∑—è, —á—Ç–æ–±—ã –∞—Ä–º–∏—è, –∫–æ—Ç–æ—Ä–∞—è —Å—Ç—Ä–æ–∏–ª–∞—Å—å –¥–≤–∞–¥—Ü–∞—Ç—å –ª–µ—Ç, —Å–µ–≥–æ–¥–Ω—è —Ç–∞–∫–∞—è: –≤—Å–µ, –º—ã –±—É–¥–µ–º —Ä–∞–±–æ—Ç–∞—Ç—å –ø–æ-–¥—Ä—É–≥–æ–º—É. –ù–∞—Å –∑–∞—Å—Ç–∞–≤–ª—è–ª–∏ –±—ã—Ç—å —Ç—É–ø—ã–º–∏ –∏ –Ω–µ –ø—Ä–∏–Ω–∏–º–∞—Ç—å –Ω–∏–∫–∞–∫–∏—Ö —Ä–µ—à–µ–Ω–∏–π, ‚Äî –ø–æ–¥—Ç–≤–µ—Ä–∂–¥–∞–µ—Ç –±—ã–≤—à–∏–π –≤–æ–µ–Ω–Ω–æ—Å–ª—É–∂–∞—â–∏–π —Ä–æ—Å—Å–∏–π—Å–∫–æ–π –∞—Ä–º–∏–∏. ‚Äî –ü–æ–ø—Ä–æ–±—É–π —Å–µ—Ä–∂–∞–Ω—Ç—É —Å–∫–∞–∂–∏, —á—Ç–æ —Ç—ã —Å—á–∏—Ç–∞–µ—à—å, —á—Ç–æ –ª—É—á—à–µ –≤–æ—Ç —Ç–∞–∫ –≤–æ—Ç. –¢–µ–±–µ –µ–±–∞–ª–æ –ø—Ä–æ—Å—Ç–æ —Å–ª–æ–º–∞—é—Ç, –µ—Å–ª–∏ –Ω–µ –∑–∞—Å—Ç—Ä–µ–ª—è—Ç —Å—Ä–∞–∑—É. –ò —Ç–∞–∫ –Ω–∞ –≤—Å–µ—Ö —É—Ä–æ–≤–Ω—è—Ö. –í–µ—Ä—Ö–æ–≤–Ω—ã–π –≥–ª–∞–≤–Ω–æ–∫–æ–º–∞–Ω–¥—É—é—â–∏–π –ø—Ä–∏–Ω–∏–º–∞–µ—Ç —Ç–æ–ª—å–∫–æ¬†‚Äû‚Äé–ø—Ä–∞–≤–∏–ª—å–Ω—ã–µ‚Äú‚Äé —Ä–µ—à–µ–Ω–∏—è ‚Äî –∞ –≤—Å–µ –æ—Å—Ç–∞–ª—å–Ω—ã–µ –¥–æ–ª–∂–Ω—ã –∏—Ö –∏—Å–ø–æ–ª–Ω—è—Ç—å. –ò –µ—Å–ª–∏ —á—Ç–æ, –æ–Ω–∏ –±—É–¥—É—Ç –Ω–µ—Å—Ç–∏ –Ω–∞–∫–∞–∑–∞–Ω–∏–µ, –Ω–µ –ø–æ—Ç–æ–º—É —á—Ç–æ —Å–≤–µ—Ä—Ö—É –¥–æ–ª–±–æ–µ–±—ã, –∞ –ø–æ—Ç–æ–º—É —á—Ç–æ¬†‚Äû‚Äé–≤—ã –ø–ª–æ—Ö–æ \[–ø—Ä–∏–∫–∞–∑—ã\] –∏—Å–ø–æ–ª–Ω—è–µ—Ç–µ, –≤—ã –Ω–µ –∏—Å–ø–æ–ª–Ω–∏—Ç–µ–ª—å–Ω—ã–µ‚Äú¬ª‚Äé, ‚Äî –≥–æ–≤–æ—Ä–∏—Ç –æ–Ω.

![–£–∫—Ä–∞—ó–Ω—Å—å–∫–∏–π –∫–æ–Ω—Ç—Ä–Ω–∞—Å—Ç—É–ø —Ç–∞ –∑–≤—ñ–ª—å–Ω–µ–Ω–Ω—è –º—ñ—Å—Ç–∞ –ë–∞–ª–∞–∫–ª—ñ—è –•–∞—Ä–∫—ñ–≤—Å—å–∫–æ—ó –æ–±–ª–∞—Å—Ç—ñ —Ç–∞ –Ω–∞–≤–∫–æ–ª–∏—à–Ω—ñ—Ö —Å—ñ–ª](data:image/svg+xml,%3Csvg%20xmlns='http://www.w3.org/2000/svg'%20viewBox='0%200%201280%20960'%3E%3C/svg%3E)

¬´–°–∞–º—ã–µ —É—Å–ø–µ—à–Ω—ã–µ –æ–ø–µ—Ä–∞—Ü–∏–∏ –∑–∞ –≤—Å—é –º–æ—é —Å–ª—É–∂–±—É –±—ã–ª–∏ —Ç–µ, –æ –∫–æ—Ç–æ—Ä—ã—Ö –∑–Ω–∞–ª–∏ —Ç–æ–ª—å–∫–æ –º—ã. –¢–æ–ª—å–∫–æ —Ç–µ –ª—é–¥–∏, –∫–æ—Ç–æ—Ä—ã–µ –≤ –Ω–µ–π —É—á–∞—Å—Ç–≤—É—é—Ç. –ü–æ—Ç–æ–º—É —á—Ç–æ —Å—Ç–æ–∏—Ç —Ç–∞–∫–∏–º –∑–∞–Ω—è—Ç—å—Å—è –∫–æ–º–∞–Ω–¥–æ–≤–∞–Ω–∏—é‚Ä¶ –ü–æ—ç—Ç–æ–º—É –∫–æ–≥–¥–∞ –º—ã —Å–∞–º–∏ —Ä–µ—à–∞–ª–∏, —á—Ç–æ –¥–µ–ª–∞—Ç—å, –Ω–µ –æ–∂–∏–¥–∞—è –∫–æ–º–∞–Ω–¥—ã —Å–≤–µ—Ä—Ö—É –∏–ª–∏ –ø–æ–∫–∞ –∫–∞—á–Ω—É—Ç —Å–≤—è–∑—å, —á—Ç–æ–±—ã —É—Ç–æ—á–Ω–∏—Ç—å, —Å–≤—è–∑–∞—Ç—å—Å—è, –∑–∞–ø—Ä–æ—Å–∏—Ç—å —Ä–∞–∑—Ä–µ—à–µ–Ω–∏–µ –Ω–∞ –≤—ã–ø–æ–ª–Ω–µ–Ω–∏–µ, —É—Ç–æ—á–Ω–µ–Ω–∏–µ –∏ –ø—Ä–æ—á—É—é —Ö–µ—Ä–Ω—é, –º—ã –≤—Å–µ–≥–¥–∞ –≤—Å–µ –≤—ã–ø–æ–ª–Ω—è–ª–∏ –Ω–∞ 100 %¬ª, ‚Äî –æ—Ç–º–µ—á–∞–µ—Ç –±—ã–≤—à–∏–π –≤–æ–µ–Ω–Ω–æ—Å–ª—É–∂–∞—â–∏–π –æ–¥–Ω–æ–≥–æ –∏–∑ —ç–ª–∏—Ç–Ω—ã—Ö –ø–æ–¥—Ä–∞–∑–¥–µ–ª–µ–Ω–∏–π –í–° –†–§.

–ù–∞–∫–∞–Ω—É–Ω–µ, 9 —Å–µ–Ω—Ç—è–±—Ä—è, –ú–∏–Ω–æ–±–æ—Ä–æ–Ω—ã¬†[–ø–æ–∫–∞–∑–∞–ª–æ](https://t.me/mod_russia/19710)
¬†–∫–∞–¥—Ä—ã –ø–µ—Ä–µ–±—Ä–æ—Å–∫–∏ –≤–æ–µ–Ω–Ω–æ–π —Ç–µ—Ö–Ω–∏–∫–∏ –≤ –•–∞—Ä—å–∫–æ–≤—Å–∫—É—é –æ–±–ª–∞—Å—Ç—å, –Ω–æ —ç—Ç–æ –ø–æ–¥–∫—Ä–µ–ø–ª–µ–Ω–∏–µ –Ω–µ –ø–æ–º–æ–≥–ª–æ –æ—Ç—Å—Ç–æ—è—Ç—å –≥–æ—Ä–æ–¥–∞. ¬´–≠—Ç–∏—Ö –ø–æ–¥–∫—Ä–µ–ø–ª–µ–Ω–∏–π –∫—Ä–∞–π–Ω–µ –Ω–µ–¥–æ—Å—Ç–∞—Ç–æ—á–Ω–æ, ‚Äî –≥–æ–≤–æ—Ä–∏—Ç –Æ—Ä–∏–π –§–µ–¥–æ—Ä–æ–≤. ‚Äî –î–∞–∂–µ –≤–µ—Ä—Ç–æ–ª–µ—Ç–∞–º–∏ –ø–µ—Ä–µ–±—Ä–∞—Å—ã–≤–∞–ª–∏ –ª–∏—á–Ω—ã–π —Å–æ—Å—Ç–∞–≤ –∏ –ª–µ–≥–∫—É—é —Ç–µ—Ö–Ω–∏–∫—É. –ù–æ —ç—Ç–æ –≤—Å–µ —Ä–∞–≤–Ω–æ, —á—Ç–æ –ø—ã—Ç–∞—Ç—å—Å—è –∏–∑ –ø–∏–ø–µ—Ç–∫–∏ –Ω–∞–ø–æ–ª–Ω–∏—Ç—å —Å—Ç–∞–∫–∞–Ω, –ø—Ä–∞–∫—Ç–∏—á–µ—Å–∫–∏ –±–µ—Å—Å–º—ã—Å–ª–µ–Ω–Ω–∞—è –∑–∞–¥–∞—á–∞¬ª.

–ê–ª–µ–∫—Å–∞–Ω–¥—Ä –ö–æ–≤–∞–ª–µ–Ω–∫–æ –æ–±—ä—è—Å–Ω—è–µ—Ç —ç—Ç–æ —Ç–µ–º, —á—Ç–æ –ø–µ—Ä–µ–±—Ä–æ—Å–∫–∞ –ø–æ–¥–¥–µ—Ä–∂–∫–∏ –±—ã–ª–∞ –ª–∏—à—å –ø—Ä–æ–ø–∞–≥–∞–Ω–¥–∏—Å—Ç—Å–∫–∏–º –∂–µ—Å—Ç–æ–º. ¬´–†–æ—Å—Å–∏–π—Å–∫–æ–π –∞—Ä–º–∏–∏ —Å—Ä–æ—á–Ω–æ –ø–æ–Ω–∞–¥–æ–±–∏–ª–æ—Å—å –¥–µ–º–æ–Ω—Å—Ç—Ä–∏—Ä–æ–≤–∞—Ç—å –Ω–µ–∫—É—é –∞–∫—Ç–∏–≤–Ω–æ—Å—Ç—å, —á—Ç–æ ‚Äû–ø–æ–º–æ—â—å –±–ª–∏–∑–∫–∞‚Äú, ‚Äû–º—ã —Å–≤–æ–∏—Ö –Ω–µ –±—Ä–æ—Å–∞–µ–º‚Äú, —è–∫–æ–±—ã –æ–Ω–∏ –≥–æ—Ç–æ–≤—ã –æ–∫–∞–∑—ã–≤–∞—Ç—å –ø–æ–¥–¥–µ—Ä–∂–∫—É —Ç–µ–º –ø–æ–¥—Ä–∞–∑–¥–µ–ª–µ–Ω–∏—è–º, –∫–æ—Ç–æ—Ä—ã–µ –æ–∫–∞–∑–∞–ª–∏—Å—å –≤ —Å–ª–æ–∂–Ω–æ–π —Å–∏—Ç—É–∞—Ü–∏–∏. –ù–æ —ç—Ç–∞ –ø–µ—Ä–µ–±—Ä–æ—Å–∫–∞ –∏–º–µ–ª–∞ –Ω–µ–æ—Ä–≥–∞–Ω–∏–∑–æ–≤–∞–Ω–Ω—ã–π, —Ö–∞–æ—Ç–∏—á–µ—Å–∫–∏–π —Ö–∞—Ä–∞–∫—Ç–µ—Ä, –æ–Ω–∞ –Ω–µ –º–æ–≥–ª–∞ –æ–±–µ—Å–ø–µ—á–∏—Ç—å –Ω–∏–∫–∞–∫–æ–π –ø–æ–¥–¥–µ—Ä–∂–∫–∏¬ª, ‚Äî –≥–æ–≤–æ—Ä–∏—Ç —ç–∫—Å–ø–µ—Ä—Ç.

–ü–æ –µ–≥–æ —Å–ª–æ–≤–∞–º, —Ç–µ –ø–æ–¥—Ä–∞–∑–¥–µ–ª–µ–Ω–∏—è, –∫–æ—Ç–æ—Ä—ã–µ –∑–∞—à–ª–∏ –≤ –∑–æ–Ω—É –±–æ–µ–≤—ã—Ö –¥–µ–π—Å—Ç–≤–∏–π –¥–ª—è –ø–æ–¥–¥–µ—Ä–∂–∫–∏, –±—ã–ª–∏ –æ–±—Ä–µ—á–µ–Ω—ã. –ú–Ω–æ–≥–∏–µ –∏–∑ –Ω–∏—Ö –¥–∞–≤–Ω—ã–º-–¥–∞–≤–Ω–æ —Ç—Ä–µ–±–æ–≤–∞–ª–∏ —Ä–æ—Ç–∞—Ü–∏–∏ –∏–ª–∏ –≤—ã–≤–æ–¥–∞ –¥–ª—è –≤–æ—Å—Å—Ç–∞–Ω–æ–≤–ª–µ–Ω–∏—è –±–æ–µ—Å–ø–æ—Å–æ–±–Ω–æ—Å—Ç–∏ –∏–∑-–∑–∞ –ø–æ–Ω–µ—Å–µ–Ω–Ω—ã—Ö –¥–æ —ç—Ç–æ–≥–æ —Å–µ—Ä—å–µ–∑–Ω—ã—Ö –ø–æ—Ç–µ—Ä—å. ¬´–í –±–ª–∏–∂–∞–π—à–µ–µ –≤—Ä–µ–º—è –º—ã –±—É–¥–µ–º —É–∑–Ω–∞–≤–∞—Ç—å –æ –±–æ–ª—å—à–æ–º –∫–æ–ª–∏—á–µ—Å—Ç–≤–µ –ø–æ–¥—Ä–∞–∑–¥–µ–ª–µ–Ω–∏–π —Ä–æ—Å—Å–∏–π—Å–∫–æ–π –∞—Ä–º–∏–∏, –∫–æ—Ç–æ—Ä—ã–µ –ø–æ–ø—Ä–æ—Å—Ç—É –ø–µ—Ä–µ—Å—Ç–∞–ª–∏ —Å—É—â–µ—Å—Ç–≤–æ–≤–∞—Ç—å, –ø–æ—Å–∫–æ–ª—å–∫—É –≤–º–µ—Å—Ç–æ –≤—ã–≤–æ–¥–∞ –Ω–∞ –≤–æ—Å—Å—Ç–∞–Ω–æ–≤–ª–µ–Ω–∏–µ –±–æ–µ—Å–ø–æ—Å–æ–±–Ω–æ—Å—Ç–∏ –∏—Ö –∫–∏–Ω—É–ª–∏ –≤ —Å–∞–º—É—é –º—è—Å–æ—Ä—É–±–∫—É, —Å–∞–º–æ–µ –∂–µ—Ä–ª–æ –±–æ–µ–≤—ã—Ö —Å—Ç–æ–ª–∫–Ω–æ–≤–µ–Ω–∏–π¬ª, ‚Äî –≥–æ–≤–æ—Ä–∏—Ç –æ–Ω.

*   [–°–∫–æ–ª—å–∫–æ –º–æ–∂–µ—Ç –¥–ª–∏—Ç—å—Å—è —ç—Ç–∞ –≤–æ–π–Ω–∞ –∏ –∫–∞–∫ –£–∫—Ä–∞–∏–Ω–µ –≤ –Ω–µ–π –ø–æ–±–µ–¥–∏—Ç—å. –ú–Ω–µ–Ω–∏–µ –¥–≤—É—Ö –≤—ã—Å–æ–∫–æ–ø—Ä–æ—Ñ–µ—Å—Å–∏–æ–Ω–∞–ª—å–Ω—ã—Ö —É–∫—Ä–∞–∏–Ω—Å–∫–∏—Ö –≥–µ–Ω–µ—Ä–∞–ª–æ–≤](https://cripo.com.ua/main/skolko-mozhet-dlytsya-eta-vojna-y-kak-ukrayne-v-nej-pobedyt-mnenye-dvuh-vysokoprofessyonalnyh-ukraynskyh-generalov/ "–°–∫–æ–ª—å–∫–æ –º–æ–∂–µ—Ç –¥–ª–∏—Ç—å—Å—è —ç—Ç–∞ –≤–æ–π–Ω–∞ –∏ –∫–∞–∫ –£–∫—Ä–∞–∏–Ω–µ –≤ –Ω–µ–π –ø–æ–±–µ–¥–∏—Ç—å. –ú–Ω–µ–Ω–∏–µ –¥–≤—É—Ö –≤—ã—Å–æ–∫–æ–ø—Ä–æ—Ñ–µ—Å—Å–∏–æ–Ω–∞–ª—å–Ω—ã—Ö —É–∫—Ä–∞–∏–Ω—Å–∫–∏—Ö –≥–µ–Ω–µ—Ä–∞–ª–æ–≤")
    

### **–ß–µ–º —Ä–æ—Å—Å–∏–π—Å–∫–æ–π –∞—Ä–º–∏–∏ –≥—Ä–æ–∑–∏—Ç –ø—Ä–æ—Ä—ã–≤ –í–°–£**

–û—Å–≤–æ–±–æ–∂–¥–µ–Ω–∏–µ –ö—É–ø—è–Ω—Å–∫–∞ –∏ –ò–∑—é–º–∞ –≤–∞–∂–Ω–æ –≤ —Å—Ç—Ä–∞—Ç–µ–≥–∏—á–µ—Å–∫–æ–º —Å–º—ã—Å–ª–µ —Ç–µ–º, —á—Ç–æ –æ–Ω–æ –æ—Ç—Ä–µ–∑–∞–µ—Ç —Ä–æ—Å—Å–∏–π—Å–∫–∏–µ –≥—Ä—É–ø–ø–∏—Ä–æ–≤–∫–∏ –æ—Ç –ø—É—Ç–µ–π —Å–Ω–∞–±–∂–µ–Ω–∏—è –∏ –æ—Ç–∫—Ä—ã–≤–∞–µ—Ç –í–°–£ –ø—É—Ç—å –Ω–∞ –õ—É–≥–∞–Ω—Å–∫–æ–µ –∏ –î–æ–Ω–µ—Ü–∫–æ–µ –Ω–∞–ø—Ä–∞–≤–ª–µ–Ω–∏–µ, –≥–æ–≤–æ—Ä–∏—Ç —É–∫—Ä–∞–∏–Ω—Å–∫–∏–π –≤–æ–µ–Ω–Ω—ã–π —ç–∫—Å–ø–µ—Ä—Ç –ê–ª–µ–∫—Å–∞–Ω–¥—Ä –ö–æ–≤–∞–ª–µ–Ω–∫–æ. ¬´–≠—Ç–∏ –≥–æ—Ä–æ–¥–∞ –≤–∞–∂–Ω—ã —Ç–µ–º, —á—Ç–æ –æ–Ω–∏ —è–≤–ª—è—é—Ç—Å—è –Ω–µ–æ—Ç—ä–µ–º–ª–µ–º–æ–π —á–∞—Å—Ç—å—é –ª–æ–≥–∏—Å—Ç–∏—á–µ—Å–∫–∏—Ö –∞—Ä—Ç–µ—Ä–∏–π –ø–æ—Å—Ç–∞–≤–æ–∫ —Ç–µ—Ö–Ω–∏–∫–∏, –º–∞—Ç–µ—Ä–∏–∞–ª—å–Ω–æ-—Ç–µ—Ö–Ω–∏—á–µ—Å–∫–æ–≥–æ –æ–±–µ—Å–ø–µ—á–µ–Ω–∏—è, –±–æ–µ–ø—Ä–∏–ø–∞—Å–æ–≤, –ª–∏—á–Ω–æ–≥–æ —Å–æ—Å—Ç–∞–≤–∞ –∫–∞–∫ –≤ –•–∞—Ä—å–∫–æ–≤—Å–∫—É—é –æ–±–ª–∞—Å—Ç—å, —Ç–∞–∫ –∏ –≤ —Ü–µ–ª–æ–º –Ω–∞ –¥–æ–Ω–±–∞—Å—Å–∫–∏–π –ø–ª–∞—Ü–¥–∞—Ä–º. –ö—É–ø—è–Ω—Å–∫ —è–≤–ª—è–µ—Ç—Å—è –æ—á–µ–Ω—å –≤–∞–∂–Ω—ã–º –ª–æ–≥–∏—Å—Ç–∏—á–µ—Å–∫–∏–º —É–∑–ª–æ–º, —Å–µ—Ä–¥—Ü–µ–º —ç—Ç–æ–π –∞—Ä—Ç–µ—Ä–∏–∏.

–ß–µ—Ä–µ–∑ –Ω–µ–≥–æ —à–ª–æ –æ–±–µ—Å–ø–µ—á–µ–Ω–∏–µ –≥–æ—Ä–æ–¥–∞ –ò–∑—é–º, –∫–æ—Ç–æ—Ä—ã–π —Å—Ç–∞–ª —Ü–µ–Ω—Ç—Ä–æ–º —Å–æ—Å—Ä–µ–¥–æ—Ç–æ—á–µ–Ω–∏—è —Å–∞–º–æ–π –±–æ–ª—å—à–æ–π –±—Ä–æ–Ω–µ—Ç–∞–Ω–∫–æ–≤–æ–π –≥—Ä—É–ø–ø—ã —Ä–æ—Å—Å–∏–π—Å–∫–∏—Ö –æ–∫–∫—É–ø–∞–Ω—Ç–æ–≤ –∑–∞ –≤—Å–µ –≤—Ä–µ–º—è –ø–æ–ª–Ω–æ–º–∞—Å—à—Ç–∞–±–Ω–æ–≥–æ –≤—Ç–æ—Ä–∂–µ–Ω–∏—è –≤ –£–∫—Ä–∞–∏–Ω—É, ‚Äî –≥–æ–≤–æ—Ä–∏—Ç —ç–∫—Å–ø–µ—Ä—Ç. ‚Äî –ò –≤—Å—è —ç—Ç–∞ –º–∞—Å—Å–∞ –¥–æ–ª–∂–Ω–∞ –±—ã–ª–∞ –∏–¥—Ç–∏ –≤ —Å—Ç–æ—Ä–æ–Ω—É –°–ª–∞–≤—è–Ω—Å–∫–∞ –∏ –ö—Ä–∞–º–∞—Ç–æ—Ä—Å–∫–∞. –°–µ–π—á–∞—Å –ø–ª–∞–Ω—ã –ø–æ –∑–∞—Ö–≤–∞—Ç—É –°–ª–∞–≤—è–Ω—Å–∫–∞ –∏ –ö—Ä–∞–º–∞—Ç–æ—Ä—Å–∫–∞ –º–æ–∂–Ω–æ —Å—á–∏—Ç–∞—Ç—å –∞–Ω–Ω—É–ª–∏—Ä–æ–≤–∞–Ω–Ω—ã–º–∏. –ü–æ—Ç–µ—Ä—è \[—Ä–æ—Å—Å–∏–π—Å–∫–æ–π –∞—Ä–º–∏–µ–π\] —Ç–∞–∫–∏—Ö –Ω–∞—Å–µ–ª–µ–Ω–Ω—ã—Ö –ø—É–Ω–∫—Ç–æ–≤ –∫–∞–∫ –ö—É–ø—è–Ω—Å–∫ –∏ –ò–∑—é–º –ø–æ–ª–Ω–æ—Å—Ç—å—é —Ä—É—à–∏—Ç —Å–∏—Å—Ç–µ–º—É –æ–±–µ—Å–ø–µ—á–µ–Ω–∏—è –¥–æ–Ω–±–∞—Å—Å–∫–æ–≥–æ –ø–ª–∞—Ü–¥–∞—Ä–º–∞ –∏ –ø–æ–∑–≤–æ–ª—è–µ—Ç –í–°–£ –≤ –¥–∞–ª—å–Ω–µ–π—à–µ–º —Ä–∞–∑–≤–∏–≤–∞—Ç—å –∫–æ–Ω—Ç—Ä–Ω–∞—Å—Ç—É–ø–∞—Ç–µ–ª—å–Ω—ã–µ –¥–µ–π—Å—Ç–≤–∏—è —É–∂–µ –Ω–µ —Ç–æ–ª—å–∫–æ –≤ –•–∞—Ä—å–∫–æ–≤—Å–∫–æ–π –æ–±–ª–∞—Å—Ç–∏, –Ω–æ –∏ –≤ –õ—É–≥–∞–Ω—Å–∫–æ–º –∏ –î–æ–Ω–µ—Ü–∫–æ–º –Ω–∞–ø—Ä–∞–≤–ª–µ–Ω–∏—è—Ö¬ª.

–í –±–ª–∏–∂–∞–π—à–∏–µ –¥–Ω–∏ –º–æ–∂–Ω–æ –æ–∂–∏–¥–∞—Ç—å, —á—Ç–æ –•–∞—Ä—å–∫–æ–≤—Å–∫–∞—è –æ–±–ª–∞—Å—Ç—å –±—É–¥–µ—Ç –æ—Å–≤–æ–±–æ–∂–¥–µ–Ω–∞, —É–≤–µ—Ä–µ–Ω —Ä–æ—Å—Å–∏–π—Å–∫–∏–π –≤–æ–µ–Ω–Ω—ã–π —ç–∫—Å–ø–µ—Ä—Ç –Æ—Ä–∏–π –§–µ–¥–æ—Ä–æ–≤. ¬´–≠—Ç–æ –Ω–µ —Ä–µ—à–∞—é—â–µ–µ —Å—Ä–∞–∂–µ–Ω–∏–µ, –Ω–æ –æ—á–µ–Ω—å –∫—Ä—É–ø–Ω—ã–π —É—Å–ø–µ—Ö –í–°–£¬ª, ‚Äî –≥–æ–≤–æ—Ä–∏—Ç –æ–Ω. –ü–æ –µ–≥–æ —Å–ª–æ–≤–∞–º, —Ç–æ–≥–¥–∞ –≤–æ–æ—Ä—É–∂–µ–Ω–Ω—ã–µ —Å–∏–ª—ã –£–∫—Ä–∞–∏–Ω—ã —Å–º–æ–≥—É—Ç –ø–µ—Ä–µ–±—Ä–æ—Å–∏—Ç—å –∑–Ω–∞—á–∏—Ç–µ–ª—å–Ω–æ–µ –∫–æ–ª–∏—á–µ—Å—Ç–≤–æ –ª–∏—á–Ω–æ–≥–æ —Å–æ—Å—Ç–∞–≤–∞ –∏ –Ω–∞ –¥—Ä—É–≥–∏–µ –Ω–∞–ø—Ä–∞–≤–ª–µ–Ω–∏—è.

### **–†–æ—Å—Å–∏–π—Å–∫–æ–π –∞—Ä–º–∏–∏ –Ω–µ —Ö–≤–∞—Ç–∞–µ—Ç —Å–∏–ª –¥–ª—è –æ–±–æ—Ä–æ–Ω—ã**

–ï—â–µ –æ–¥–Ω–æ –Ω–µ –º–µ–Ω–µ–µ –≤–∞–∂–Ω–æ–µ –Ω–∞–ø—Ä–∞–≤–ª–µ–Ω–∏–µ, –Ω–∞ –∫–æ—Ç–æ—Ä–æ–º –ø—Ä–æ–¥–æ–ª–∂–∞—é—Ç –Ω–∞—Å—Ç—É–ø–∞—Ç—å —Å–∏–ª—ã –í–°–£, ‚Äî –∫–æ–Ω—Ç—Ä–æ–ª–∏—Ä—É–µ–º—ã–π —Ä–æ—Å—Å–∏–π—Å–∫–∏–º–∏ –≤–æ–π—Å–∫–∞–º–∏ –ø–ª–∞—Ü–¥–∞—Ä–º –Ω–∞ –ø—Ä–∞–≤–æ–º –±–µ—Ä–µ–≥—É –î–Ω–µ–ø—Ä–∞ –≤ –•–µ—Ä—Å–æ–Ω—Å–∫–æ–π –æ–±–ª–∞—Å—Ç–∏. –£–∫—Ä–∞–∏–Ω—Å–∫–æ–µ –∫–æ–Ω—Ç—Ä–Ω–∞—Å—Ç—É–ø–ª–µ–Ω–∏–µ –Ω–∞—á–∞–ª–æ—Å—å —Ç–∞–º 29 –∞–≤–≥—É—Å—Ç–∞. –í —Ç–æ—Ç –¥–µ–Ω—å, –ø–æ¬†[–¥–∞–Ω–Ω—ã–º](https://www.facebook.com/watch/?v=1018539645523163)
¬†–æ–ø–µ—Ä–∞—Ç–∏–≤–Ω–æ–π –≥—Ä—É–ø–ø–∏—Ä–æ–≤–∫–∏ –í–°–£ ¬´–ö–∞—Ö–æ–≤–∫–∞¬ª, –µ–π —É–¥–∞–ª–æ—Å—å ¬´–ø—Ä–æ—Ä–≤–∞—Ç—å –ø–µ—Ä–≤—É—é –ª–∏–Ω–∏—é –æ–±–æ—Ä–æ–Ω—ã¬ª –≤ –•–µ—Ä—Å–æ–Ω—Å–∫–æ–π –æ–±–ª–∞—Å—Ç–∏. ¬´109 –ø–æ–ª–∫ ‚Äû–î–ù–†‚Äú –æ—Ç–æ—à–µ–ª —Å–æ —Å–≤–æ–∏—Ö –ø–æ–∑–∏—Ü–∏–π, —Ä–æ—Å—Å–∏–π—Å–∫–∏–µ –¥–µ—Å–∞–Ω—Ç–Ω–∏–∫–∏, –∫–æ—Ç–æ—Ä—ã–µ –±—ã–ª–∏ –∏—Ö –ø–æ–¥–¥–µ—Ä–∂–∫–æ–π, —Å–±–µ–∂–∞–ª–∏ —Å –ø–æ–ª—è –±–æ—è¬ª, ‚Äî¬†[–≥–æ–≤–æ—Ä–∏–ª–æ—Å—å](https://www.facebook.com/watch/?v=1018539645523163)
¬†–≤ —Å–æ–æ–±—â–µ–Ω–∏–∏. 4 —Å–µ–Ω—Ç—è–±—Ä—è –í–°–£¬†[—É—Å—Ç–∞–Ω–æ–≤–∏–ª–∏](https://www.facebook.com/kirill.timoshenko/posts/5588117717898633)
¬†—É–∫—Ä–∞–∏–Ω—Å–∫–∏–π —Ñ–ª–∞–≥ –≤ –∫—Ä—É–ø–Ω–æ–º –Ω–∞—Å–µ–ª–µ–Ω–Ω–æ–º –ø—É–Ω–∫—Ç–µ –í—ã—Å–æ–∫–æ–ø–æ–ª—å–µ.
